A very weak story overall. While Dontnod seems to want to tackle difficult and emotional tales, its pretty clear that their writing department isn't up to the task.

The game starts by introducing one of its two protagonists, a trans man named Tyler who 

The key mystery of why the twins' mother tried to kill Tyler? 

What remains is a drawn out game where you're solving a mystery that barely makes sense, following characters who are difficult to sympathize with (both of them often getting into pointless bickering with each other and those around them), with gameplay that proceeds at a snail's pace and whose biggest moments could have easily been predicted hours earlier.

I see a lot of people who seem inclined to support this game because of all the hate it got from transphobes. Despite the stupid reasons they may have for disliking the game, I advise against hailing this as some sort of milestone in story telling and representation. The game uses it's LGBT-positive elements as bait to get positive coverage and reviews, only to cast them aside in the first 2 hours all so Dontnod could tell a story that's mediocre even by gaming standards.

I got this game for free and I still feel ripped off. Do yourself a favor and don't bother.

The plot is fairly good, nothing groundbreaking but easy enough to get invested in. For the last few we ended up just googling the answers because it was so dull flicking through a storybook trying to find details like "did the goblins scratch the moose's back?". There were several puzzles (like the computer password) which we could solve without having to find the 'proper' clue for it, but we still had to find clues and items in the 'correct' order to unlock the next bit of dialogue/cutscene. The characters seem to be pretty slow in general compared to the player, not putting two-and-two together puzzlewise or plotwise.

The game has nice visuals, but I feel that they sacrificed pace and content for it. There are far too many moments where the characters stop and have a long, fairly uninteresting conversation in front of some picturesque view. Very obvious that the devs were more interested in going "ooh look how pretty our game is" rather than focusing on engagement.

If you're considering playing this game please know that there is very little replay value, so you'll almost definitely just be doing the one playthrough which is about 12 hours. I'd recommend waiting for a sale, I would have kicked off if I'd paid full price for this.

9 people found this review helpful 1

Not Recommended
6.3 hrs on record
Posted: 6 June, 2021
Product received for free

This review will have minimal spoilers, which will not spoil the story outright, but may touch on a couple story bits and sequences. These spoilers are not marked.


The Story
(Disclaimer: I got the max bond + don’t believe the original memory ending (which is the “best” ending); I did not encounter or watch the other endings.)
The writing is very akin to the Life is Strange series, with that classic “American young adults transparently being written by 40-year old French dudes” aspect in the dialogue (“get all Smeagol” being a notable highlight), but it has one major distinguishing factor versus Dontnod’s other works: it’s extremely slow-paced, with a lot of unnecessary padding to boot -- for example, there is a thirty-minute section wherein you do housekeeping. There are a lot of gratuitous twists, with both chapter 1 and 2 throwing anemic screwballs towards the end of each of them in order to keep the drama going in spite of not much of anything really happening.
Since we’re discussing gratuitous things, the superpower that the game revolves around, specifically the memories and Alyson and Tyler’s telepathic link, are both insubstantial and not really explored in any way. The memories are just that -- remembering things that happened (including having Alyson and Tyler’s memories not sync up), which I’m sure both you and I have; the only thing the characters have over us is that they can render it in 3D. Their memories don’t even sync up and have significant differences, which makes this fantastical power seem very mundane. The story could have removed these magical powers entirely, and it would have largely been the same, a sharp (and ultimately negative) contrast to the rest of Dontnod’s games.
The story itself meanders and doesn’t do all that much until the tail end of each chapter. Much of what happens is supposed to be character-bonding moments, which ultimately comes across as filler (see below on the characters).
As a consequence, the game feels directionless until it manages to stumble into its climax. The climax itself is merely competent, and doesn’t feel like a grand finale or anything particularly special.


On The Stuff With Tyler
I’m not going to talk too much about this, because frankly I lack the credentials to discuss it in a thorough manner.
The transgender aspect of Tyler was handled quite well, and as someone who is not transgender I would consider it an interesting insight.
Despite this, it doesn’t redeem this game for me, and it doesn’t justify trudging through the lackluster story to experience these story bits.


The Characters
The characters are fairly weak altogether. Tyler acts like a jerk at multiple points, but outside of him the characters don’t really feel like they have any sort of defining characteristics that would cause them to have staying power within my memory. They aren't especially one-note (or really that grating), but they aren't interesting, either.
This is compounded with the fact that the voice acting is very mediocre in this game, with the majority of the cast coming across as apathetic in their performances; only Alyson managed to come across as solid. Tyler is especially notable in terms of weak voice acting, as even when he’s trying to sound impassioned, he doesn’t really have a lot of emotion in him.


Technical Aspects
I didn’t encounter many bugs, especially major ones such as softlocks or crazy animation glitches. I think I encountered one animation bug where a character was randomly static during their idle animation, and I only got a couple audio glitches towards the end of the game where a few lines of dialogue randomly freaked out.
In terms of graphics, this is probably the best-looking Dontnod game. That isn’t saying much (especially when you compare it to Life Is Strange and Before The Storm, which are getting much-needed visual remasters), but it’s reasonably pretty, and the rural environment lets them make nice landscapes to serve as backdrops (though the game had a couple too many "look how pretty our game is" shots for my tastes, but that's just a nitpick).
Speaking of art, the art with the Book of Goblins is very nice, with a great balance of refinement and style. It makes me wish that the whole game was expressed through that fairy tale storybook style instead of the decent at best 3D replica of the real world. A game that was built around that vibe would certainly have been much more interesting, and would have been a fun break from the typical Life is Strange formula. Alas, it was not to be.


The Actual Mechanics
As is to be expected from a game that is as story-focused as this one, the gameplay isn't intensive or even much of a priority, and for the most part it's walking around to get to the next story bit (which, for the record, was anticipated and is completely fine by me). The puzzles aren’t too rough; I only brute-forced the ones where I had to consult the Book of Goblins to solve (specifically the door puzzle in chapter 1 and the loft puzzle in chapter 3) out of lack of patience rather than getting stuck on them.
There were three minigames, and only the second one where you try to calm Alyson down during a panic attack is the only one that came across as obtuse and clunky. If you’ve ever played a video game before, you shouldn’t have any trouble with them. They’re alright change-ups, but not really common enough to be anything more than short breaks.


TL;DR and Conclusion: If you like the Life Is Strange games, you will probably like this one. If you don’t like those games, you will probably not like this one. If you’re one of those people that play these games for the “so bad it’s good” factor, the extremely slow pace outweighs what slight amusement can be eked out from it.


Final rating: 3/10


"...Ain't nothin' but a heartache" - The Backstreet Boys

Not Recommended
11.1 hrs on record
Posted: 19 March, 2021
Feel free to follow my review page! and my twitch https://www.twitch.tv/nightserg

The gist of it:
Tell Me Why is a narrative-focused game, with not much going for it even in the plot department, an average mystery that will slowly unveil itself without any dangerous outcomes.

👍 The good parts:
+The twins and most of the cast do a fine job at carrying the plot.
+Locations are small but quite detailed and nice to look at.

👎The bad parts:
-The shtick of the game or the mystery fails to shock or even surprise you.
-Little to no gameplay with just a very few amount of puzzles.

Story
It's hard to talk about this particular game without spoiling some things but I'll obviously keep them minor as much as possible. The game starts with one of the twins admitting to killing their mother and then it fast forwards a lot of years in the future when they're more mature.

Yes before you ask, this game has a huge focus half the game on the issues of transitioning from female to male for one of the twins, Tyler, and how he is perceived by the others, and how troubling was his fast as a kid especially for his mother. The other twin Alyson has her own issues, dealing with the past and as you progress through the game, more is revealed as to what happened that led to the death of their mother.

Initially, the game will give you an impression that more is going on but unfortunately that's not going to be the case, at least not what you'd expect from a DONTNOD game. The plot is very safe and very much average without any real stakes in the choices you make and without any tragic or dramatic outcomes.

Honestly, when you finish it, it comes down to just being a story about some twins that simply just forgot what happened in the past and that's it. Even their power which allows them to talk to each other through their thoughts as well as relive some of their memories feels very gimmicky.

Story rating: 6.5/10

Gameplay
There's not much to talk about the gameplay as there's not much to do in the game besides clicking on some objects and a few puzzles which revolve around you reading and figuring out what to press.

Gameplay in this particular genre needs a drastic change, something to push it forward, else most people just won't bother, especially when the plot itself isn't that great. The first Life is Strange at least had an interesting time mechanic which really felt like a part of the story like it had an impact but Tell Me Why's power mechanic is just there to push the story forward, to make sense of it without any real dangers to it.

You have moments in the story where you can pick between two memories and have to decide which one you feel is the right one but ultimately neither is wrong which makes the choices pointless.

Gameplay rating: 5.5/10

Audio
A story-focused game needs to have good or above voice acting and suffice to say Tell Me Why does a decent job at it. Some characters sound weird and out of place but most of them especially Alyson do a wonderful job at creating emotion. Tyler is mostly passive and rarely has any good moments but his sister goes through some really tough emotional stuff and pulls her heart out which is something I have to give props to.

The music is very scarce, only a few songs here and there but they're ok and as for the sound effects and everything else related, nothing really out of the ordinary.

Audio rating: 7.5/10

Graphics, performance and tech analysis
The graphics and art style are well crafted and while the locations you visit are very small with no depth to the level design whatsoever they do look quite detailed and fit quite well with the plot. It was pleasing, relaxing, to explore some of the locations especially their cabin, which had this warmth to it.

As for performance, I had absolutely no issues running the game, and I encountered no bugs whatsoever.

Graphics, performance and tech analysis score: 8/10

Conclusion
Look, Tell Me Why is not really a bad game but it just does not have a good enough plot to make it worth recommending, and with little to no gameplay to compensate why would you consider it? If it's very cheap, go ahead and buy it if you're bored but if you have a huge backlog of games, just focus on them instead, it's a dead year after all :)

Final score: 6.8/10

Tell me why is a third person game where you take on the role of two siblings, Alison and Tyler. They go back to the house they grew up in only to find that their memories were not what they thought.

Pros:
Good animations
Simple controls
Excellent graphics
Voice acting is very good

Cons:
Story is weak
The ending is very predicable
Very Linear
Puzzles are uninteresting
There is an insane amount of reading
Very short game for the price
Choices don't matter that much
Several long pauses in conversations
More like a walking simulator
Liberal overtones

I would have to say that the best thing about this game was the excellent graphics. You can tell that a lot a work went into it. I just wish the developers would have spent more time improving the story instead of the graphics.

I can't go to much into the bad points of this game because it would take too long to read. So I'll give you the top 3 and I'll abbreviate.

First, the story is uninteresting. For a short time, it seemed that there may be some kind of supernatural element that may be at play which really interested me but, ultimately, when you find out what it is, it's very disappointing.

Second, the big reveal was so predicable then when it happened, I simply said, “Called it.”

Third, I've played a lot of games that had way too much reading but this game takes the cake. My lord, it is insane and most of it is filler. Useless information that you don't need or it was rehashing information that you already knew.

Okay, this is more of a pet peeve than a con but the entire game is laced with liberal overtones. Some of the points I agree with, others I don't. Here or there, this crap does not belong in gaming because I felt I was being preached to. I don't want to be preached to, I want a game I enjoy but the developers fell well short of that goal if it ever was a goal.

At the time of this review, Tell me why was selling for $29.99. That's way to much for this game. Even if it were good, it's too much because of the short length of game play.

Sock
0
8 people found this review helpful 1

Not Recommended
1.8 hrs on record
Posted: 17 October, 2024
Before you point your finger and say "He hates the LGBTQ+ community," let me say that's not why I don't like this game.

One of the reasons is the graphics. The game looks...fine. But there is something about the characters that makes it really hard listen to the dialogue instead of just staring at the face. The lipsync feels off and facial expression just feels empty of emotion. The eyes feel especially off. The characters (specifically Alyson for some reason) are never actually looking at anything. In the scenes where you can move the camera, it's really distracting.

Me second gripe is the story. It isn't the fact that it revolves around a trans guy, it's just not interesting. Admittedly, I've only played the first episode, and some of the second. I will probably finish it, but unlike other episodic games like The Walking Dead, these episodes aren't really interesting and don't push me to keep playing. I also feel like there are a bunch of plot holes that are really distracting (like why did Tyler get convicted if his mother was stabbed in the back, and why doesn't Alyson remember that?). I'm sure some of these get answered later in the story, but the way it's presented makes me confused about the plot instead of excited to find out the answer.

My third gripe is the gameplay. I'm a massive Telltale fan, and this game is very similar in that regard. It's just that there's a few gameplay design choices that feel useless and make the game more tedious. The first one I want to bring up is holding LT (I play on controller) to answer a question. Why is this a thing? I actually want someone to explain why this is a thing. Why is there an extra step when answering dialogue? This serves no purpose and honestly hurt my playthrough. The second is The Book of Goblins. Story-wise, this is actually a cool addition. Gameplay-wise, it makes the experience feel much more like a chore. Throughout the game, I feel forced to study the vague lines of a book to progress. In the first episode you get a choice to either do the puzzle or skip it, but hurt your relationship with Alyson. The developers should not have introduced that at all, since it introduces the idea that puzzles are optional and aren't necessary to progress. If the player learns that and keeps on hurting their relationships, it eventually hurts the story.

And that is why I don't like this game. Me and many others got it free in June, because the developer's history with games like Life Is Strange. That's right. I got this game because of the developers, not the game itself.

All in all, this game had potential. I can see another game like this, that could almost go against Life Is Strange. But when you make a game, you have to make it interesting, and keep it interesting. I'm not saying this happened, but it's becoming too common in the entertainment industry: the developers need to stop focusing on the fact that it's a game with a transgender protagonist, but rather on making a good game with a good story.

Here's the kicker that the gaming community really can't take: if you like this game, I respect that. Yeah that's right. I'm not gonna judge you or laugh at you for playing this game. It was YOUR CHOICE to play this. Not mine, or anyone else's. NOT ME, OR ANYBODY ELSE HAVE THE RIGHT TO TELL YOU HOW TO SPEND YOUR MONEY. If you like this game and disagree with me criticism, THATS OKAY.

Ok, that's about it.

Tell Me Why

A broken game.

Purchased Cost: Free

I currently considered 'Tell Me Why' to be broken with a game ending bug that has been reported by numerous players for the last several months.

I've been playing video games since the ZX Spectrum and I can count on one hand game ending bugs I've experienced. Unfortunately 'Tell Me Why' is one of these games.

In Chapter 3 (Scene: Paternity Test) it is impossible to continue the story as the game gets stuck in a loop. Sitting down to eat Cobbler whilst waiting for Dee to finish her report in the police station doesn't trigger the next scene and it's impossible to continue from here.


Tell Me Why 
A Screenshot of Tell Me Why
By: harv


This issue still remains unresolved. I've previously purchased 'Remember Me', 'Vampyr', 'Life is Strange' and 'Before the Storm' from DontNod but will no longer support them until this is resolved and have now removed 'Life is Strange 2' from my wishlist.

My current advice is to ignore this game and developer for future releases. I will of course amend this review if they fix the issue.

RisingPhönix
0
17 people found this review helpful 1

Not Recommended
28.0 hrs on record
Posted: 17 December, 2020
I'd been thinking a lot whether to recommend this game or not, and to my great surprise, I chose not to.
Of course, not all elements of the game were disappointing. The game is really good starting point for DONTNOD to create another exciting franchise. The pretty good graphics depicting the picturesque Alaskan small town environment and nature were really charming, and this made the exploration of areas a pleasant experience. I also loved the design of the interiors. On the flip side, the playable character movement animation seems unnatural and excessively shaky. Sometimes, there is even a wind effect applied to clothing when a protagonist is inside a building with doors and windows closed. A few graphical glitches may also be encountered.

The sound and the music are pretty decent too. Nothing to complain about, but the soundtrack wasn’t memorable enough to stick with me after finishing the story, unlike the pieces in the previous games, even the one single song from the Awesome Adventures of Captain spirit stayed with me for a while.

The idea behind the game is exciting and definitely worth expanding. I liked the memory hunting mechanics, almost straight from Remember Me. Too bad that the memories . I also appreciate the effort the authors put into the Book of Goblins, especially the artwork.
The story has a lot of potential. I loved the shocking plot twists at the closing parts of the chapters. I liked the main protagonists - the Ronan siblings, and the introduction of the transgender character didn’t feel forced. The character seemed so natural and relatable as they would as a real person. It surprised me that the story involved  characteristic of the LiS series, but this time the  affected only the two main protagonists and not the entire environment around them. It is also an interesting revelation that the two characters remember the past so differently. Their personalities also differ much enough to make their interactions fascinating.

Despite the fact that this game isn’t a Life is Strange franchise entry, it pretty much feels like it. And here's why:
• It has an episodic structure and features the choice and consequence mechanics.
• It introduces two closely related main protagonists who know each other really well working together on a mutual problem. A nice diversification from the LiS franchise is the fact that throughout the game, you have the chance to play as both of them, not only one for the entire game.
• the action of the game takes place in a small remote town in contemporary USA, which happens to be their hometown and they come back to reunite after several years being apart, although the purpose of this reunion is different.
• There is  in Tell Me Why.  What makes this  different than the ones that LiS protagonists have, is the fact that it is shared by both the twins and it cannot affect anyone else.
• Its narrative focuses on the past and involves flashbacks from the past. The two main characters carry out an investigation to reveal a mystery from the past, just like in LiS1. The characters may also resort to crime to obtain necessary items or information, and the interviews and interrogations are based on previously gathered intel, and their results vary on the basis of previous choices.
• It features LGBT characters.
• The siblings’ mother .
• It has the same unique art style characteristic of the LiS series.
• The story is told like a fable from the Book of Goblins, just like the story of the Wolf Brothers in LiS2.
• Just like in the LiS series, we’ve got a set of collectible objects of sentimental value.

So, what is wrong with the game? The first noticeable flaw is the pacing. Too slow at one time and too fast at another. We don’t have the option to choose the speed of movement - the characters walk or run at times specified by the game. Sometimes it is annoying that we move so slowly, and sometimes we move too quickly to spot interesting details.

Yet, what is the most heart breaking for me is the poor character introduction and relation. There are just a few secondary characters in the game, and even fewer have significance to the story. Their backstories aren’t fully explained, and the relations and generally shallow. I started to have such issue on my first playthrough of LiS2, but in that game, we were constantly on the move, running from a threat, and here we are in one location - a childhood town, full of memories, and people we know really well, well we are supposed to know them really well, but the developers don’t really allow us to.

This could be solved by introducing flashbacks from closer and further past, depicting significant moments in the twins' relation with every each of the characters. Sometimes we are forced to make choices that severely impact the relations between us and other characters before we even know who they are, for example when  That's simply absurd.

Furthermore, the  seems really forced and out of place. Engaging in such a relation under the circumstances depicted in the game just didn’t feel natural, and, of course I chose not to, but there really should not be such option in the first place.

Last but not least, the characters fail to convey emotions and behaviours typical of human beings under certain, especially stressful circumstances. The moment that it most obvious occurred when  That is just one instance of this issue that I happen to remember best, but there are at least a few more.

To sum up, the game seems to be a failed LiS game, that for business needs was rebranded, not to ruined the great esteem and reputation of the franchise and sold as a different game because it was in the middle of development and yet unfinished when the publisher decided that it was the time of release. This would also explain the relatively low price on the day of the premiere, which is justifiable, given the quality of the game.
The game isn't terrible, it is quite decent, but it is a DONTNOD game and you don’t expect anything but the best and most unique story, complex characters, great music and original art style, which is really disappointing about Tell Me Why.

Not Recommended
12.6 hrs on record
Posted: 12 September, 2020
Product received for free

The issue of identity is handled with more respect than the hamfisted two-dimensional tokenized way it usually is and there is not nearly as much "cringe" as there was in Life Is Strange. The remote Alaskan setting is compelling.

Unfortunately, the game is way too long, even though it's much shorter (for the same price) as Life Is Strange and Life Is Strange 2 (15hrs versus 8+hrs). The padding should have been removed. (for instance, you spend 10+ minutes choosing what items to pack or not, but it isn't relevant to anything and has no consequence, the animations seem needlessly slow, the conversations drag on in a way that doesn't progress the story at all). This entire game should have only been a single four hour episode -- and even then it might have been lacking, simply because of the story and it's resolution.

It's also frustrating that the "children's stories" which play an absolutely integral part to the game are not narrated. There are twenty of them and you just have to read them silently on the screen, like some Mass Effect codex. If these had been narrated by the siblings, it would have been so terrific!

I liked the world this game took place in and a lot of the characters -- even though we only get to meet a few of them, but I found myself having the same reaction my audience did at the end of each chapter (and the game), which was "wait, is that it?!"

10 people found this review helpful 0

Not Recommended
10.1 hrs on record
Posted: 26 December, 2020
Underwhelming, but I came in with high expectations after having enjoyed Life is Strange. I won't really compare the two, as someone else did that, but I'll just say that this one doesn't hold a candle to LiS.

The good:
I liked the trans inclusion parts. It wasn't just shoved in for feel good sjw points, but there was a vital plot point for it. Story-wise it was refreshing to see something like this. I loved some of the artwork. The voice acting was good. The location was interesting. There was a lot of hard work that went into worldbuilding the town, and I really appreciated diving into it all. For example, there's a small police case sideplot that gets revolved along with the main story, and it was kinda neat to get closure on it even if it had no real impact on anything.

The bad.
Story was predictable as all hell. I had the gist of what happened by the end of the first chapter, and the rest of it was just filling in the mystery gaps. By the time the characters found out about some big reveal, it just felt like they were way behind the curve. The stakes weren't high here, either. Tension was low. Emotional impact was low to moderate. There was a TON of unnecessary bits of story that just served to waste time. Like the romance bits. I shipped them, of course, but man what a waste of time. Mentioning a waste of time, there were several other 'twists' in the story that had little impact on the rest of the story. These bits really surprised me and made some sense on the backstory, but ultimately it changed nothing.

Most of the problems in the story stemmed from how childish the two main characters were behaving. It was almost a coming of age type story as the player needs to force them to act like a patient, empathetic, reasonable adult in order to get the better scenes, and to be honest, these choices are almost obvious.

Honestly, if I were a thirteen year old having not played LiS, I would've been impressed with this game. I probably wouldn't have seen the "twists" coming a mile away, I might've identified with the two "young adults" much better, but I didn't.

Don't get me wrong. It isn't a bad game. It's a watered-down Life is Strange, but much less interesting and way less exciting.

Sigh... the more DONTNOD games I play the more I realise that "Life is Strange" was a complete fluke. Full disclaimer I have only played the first chapter as it was free, and from what I can tell this game tries to go for the LGBTQ angle but fails to explore it in any realistic way.
If I have to give a few pointers I would ditch the supernatural ESP stuff for this game. The supernatural feature worked in "Life is Strange" because Max was a quiet timid girl and it was interesting to see what happens when you give someone like that time travel powers. Here in this game however it just feels random and doesn't add anything to the story.
I also would have preferred it if Tyler didn't connect with Alyson after being separated for 10 years, maybe have him be completely different to what Alyson remembered and reconnect over time after overcoming huddles like you would see in a drama.
With regards to the LGBTQ theme, you want to illustrate both of sides of the extremities i.e. show the bigots as well as the the overly sensitive types (fyi both have negative impacts on people dealing with gender issues). Maybe highlight how differently people in their town treats Tyler after his switch, or even better show us why lead to Tyler deciding to identify as a man (which would of course require some research and better writers).

Overall this left a disappointing first impression, and at this point I'm turned off by DONTNOD games which is such a sad thing to admit after the masterpiece that was "Life is Strange"

Not Recommended
2.5 hrs on record
Posted: 5 August, 2022
Product received for free

This aint it chief. Lightning doesn't strike twice.

I wanted to like this game. Big fan of the original LiS (not so much LiS2 which was also a bit of a flop unfortunately). I'd love for DONTNOD to have their own IP (that Square Enix doesn't own) that's GOOD. Unfortunately Deck Nine has done a better job on LiS: True Colours than both this and LiS2. What happened to your writers DONTNOD? Programming/art is on point as far as I can see.

All the dialogue felt so stilted, the "superpower" just feels awkward - half the "past" scenes don't really add much and the talking to eachother part just seems to interupt normal conversations while everyone just stares at eachother awkwardly. The main characters don't even seem all that surprised to have these abilities. Compare this to LiS which has Chloe hyping the whole thing up (not to mention rewinding time fitting perfectly as a game mechanic). The "hook" really isn't here with viewing the past because its really just not that interesting.

The dialogue choices don't really seem to matter much and sometimes I didn't even want to select one of the two offered choices.

I do love the Alaskan scenery, the graphics are excellent. For some reason they thought making you sit through a 10 minute ferry ride right at the start of the game would be fun for some reason - they're really padding the game time. Not a whole lot of substance to interact with, you're just trapped on the boat. There's a later scene where you're literally picking up items to buy in a grocery store - it seems pointless.

The puzzle in Episode 1 with the story book and the locks on the door was just needlessly frustrating. "Here, have a book with 1000s of words of children's stories, use it to solve this lock!" - honestly less time to brute force it. Very lazy puzzle design - a far cry from most adventure games with regular puzzles throughout.

How every single person in town reacted was almost identical to each other. There's no personality here. The game feels very on rails and there aren't a heap of NPCs to interact with at any one time and even when you do its the one/two liner type interactions. There's no dialogue type puzzles where you "unlock" additional choices with other characters.

The voices used in some of the past interactions seems to switch randomly. I'm assuming they're both roughly 18 in the "present", 8 years old in the "past" but it feels like the voice actor swapped in some of the past scenes. Sometimes its a young girl's voice, other times a young boy's voice. They also drop the line that Tyler only started testosterone 3 years prior to the present. It makes no sense.

The game (and the developers) really want to push an agenda about one of the main characters being trans. Every NPC seems to react to THAT rather than the fact that Tyler KILLED HIS MOTHER which I'm sure everyone in a small town would have known her somewhat well. The game is set in 2015 or so but acts like its set in 2022 (or even later considering how most people react to this "news"). The redneck style guy in the house reminded me of the one dimensional "bigot" type characters in LiS2 - simply there to make a political point rather than tell a story.

Meanwhile Tyler has been able to come and go from his "institution" (juvie?) for the past 3 years and didn't go back home which is seemingly across the lake. For someone that has gone through all this trauma, Tyler reacts surprisingly mildly to absolutely everything and is seemingly well adjusted - this is very congruent to his circumstances. This character isn't fleshed out at all. Not to mention the sister being incredibly bland herself.

Adding LGBT themes is fine, DONTNOD has even done this well in other games. Unfortunately tacking it onto any old story doesn't make that story GOOD.

I'm just glad I didn't pay for this. Did not finish.

delaroca
0
6 people found this review helpful 0

Not Recommended
12.8 hrs on record
Posted: 27 February, 2022
Fairly disappointing, casual drama story, which feels like a novel that wasn't adapted to game format, but rather remained a novel. It's a 3D point-and-click "adventure" game, although there is not much sense of an adventure, as the story follows people dealing with their traumas and exploring their past. The gameplay consists mostly of searching several recurring locations for interactive objects and annoyingly adjusting the camera to select them, watching people chat about all kinds of unrelated things, waiting for UI animations to let you select a response 6 seconds after a question is asked, and waiting for character animations to complete (their slowness makes RDR2 jealous). While most animations look alright and there is a large variety of full-body movements throughout the scenes, facial animations looked very uncanny to me; maybe because only mouths, eyeballs and eyebrows get to move, and all in just one direction, which, considering the otherwise high-fidelity art style, makes characters look like puppets. This is especially jarring in emotional scenes, which look completely out of place. The primary themes of this game, including traumas, transgender identity, suicide, etc. are merely mentioned, and not explored, leaving the story much without substance. In my view, merely featuring a gay character in a drama story is insufficient to make it the holy book of LGBT communities this game pretends to be. It also pretends to be a choice-heavy game, and while yes, lots of choices matter, most are barely consequential and do not change where the story goes, rather, they usually change the specific words characters will use, or photos that will appear in-game. And it's definitely not a role-playing game, all player choices are completely arbitrary, and you do not know enough background about characters to make a conscious decision about their role in the story. So they usually boil down to "be nice / be a jerk" or "reunite / reject". You get to choose the story you wish to see, but you don't really influence character development. The pacing of the game is really off. It's a relatively chill story, no action, no (actual) mysteries, no motives, just watch along. So it is intentionally very very slow. Yet besides all scenes being fully voiced and animated, every 2 minutes you are hit with ten document you need to read in detail to be able to continue the story. I don't mind reading stuff in games, but the way it interrupts character interactions all the time completely kills the dynamics of each scene. Not to mention the game literally features a child's stories book with around 20 fantasy stories for kids, which the player is supposed to read in entirety to be able to solve in-game puzzles and understand all metaphores. Really feels out of place. Also, with the game being so directly founded in reality, the occasional paranormal / supernatural themes were completely unnecessary; the marketing materials made it seem like it's going to be a major element of the game, while it was not, and the story would have worked just as well without them, making them redundant and unwelcome.
The parts I liked about the game were the highly-detailed art style, gorgeous Alaskan scenery which can be admired in all areas, the absolutely brilliant performance by Alyson's VA, and the pretty good soundtrack.
My playtime is not representative as I took pauses, there is around 6-8h of content.

I was lured in to see Alaska's snow capped mountains and rippling waterfalls, bears and whales, arts of Tlingit, Haida, Tsimshian and Eyak artists.

The first 30 minutes was very satisfying.

Especially on the ferry boat, I was able to see cedar trees and shore pines on snow covered mountains, soaking up the serenity of that peaceful lake, and witnessed the humpback whale jumping out of the water.

After arriving the Mary Ann's house, it was a small adventure to figure out how to find way to enter the house, interesting but not difficult.

Yet once inside of the house, the nightmare began.

I have to go through every props, digging out stories behind it, read the whole fairy tale book, and found the diary, transgender child education book, it was sad and depressed. What made it worse is the recap of Tyler's childhood story. It began to grow into a very unpleasant feeling that I was trapped in this story, inside of this house, and unable to go outside to take a breath.

The emotion has made this game so heavy that I got to quit the game to take a break.

When I found out that 95% of game time, you'll be indoors, talking to Alyson - that's my last straw, uninstalled the game.

Maybe it's a good story, for those who want to experience Tyler's life and inner conflicts, but it's not for me.

I was a little disappointed not being able to explore Delos Crossing town, and the designs of local artists were buried under the heavy story-line. The game team could have done a better job.

Product received for free

[CONTAINS MINOR SPOILERS for TMW, LiS1, LiS2]

Marginally better story than Life is Strange 2 (disaster), but overall uninteresting and still retains the cringeworthy and interminably long chapter recaps (this time it's goblins instead of wolves). The short, simple recaps from Life is Strange 1 were the best and should never have been changed.

+ Tell Me Why's music is flawless. Dontnod always chooses good soundtracks.

+ Graphically stunning. A huge leap forward from LiS2.

+ Representation of minorities (trans man in this case) is good though I prefer the subtlety of LiS1 (and media that isn't explicit in general).

+ Can skip cutscenes after initial playthrough (yay).

- Dontnod tends to tackle questions of morality in their games, which I'm always interested in. However, I struggled to feel any major impact from the decisions presented in TMW. The only scene which makes a deep impression in my view is the 'negative' ending. The remaining choices and consequences felt extremely bland, and more like jaded filler material that consumed the overwhelming majority of every episode.

- As another reviewer mentioned, the narrative conflict is already resolved within the first episode. The audience is made aware of the protagonist's misunderstanding/confusion over past memories, and that the supposed antagonist was maligned unjustly (the FAQ section on the official TMW website confirms this to be true). This instantly kills player curiosity and makes the road ahead a dreary one. LiS2 had a similar narrative error: forcing players to initiate a long, tedious and ultimately pointless journey across the country to avoid incrimination when there is absolutely no proof that staying put would have resulted in it, and basically spoiling the ending. Compare TMW and LiS2 with LiS1, which gives the player hints but never states definitively what will happen and also manages to shock the majority with a great plot twist.

Prince of the Land of Stench!
115 products in account
1
5 people found this review helpful
1 person found this review funny 0

Not Recommended
7.2 hrs on record
Posted: 29 June, 2021
Product received for free

Chapter 2 done, got it for free during June ... and I will complete the 3rd chapter, just because, but damn, I feel like my time's been robbed.

Let's put aside the "main issue" people are going to have with this game (apparently), namely the transgender protagonist. I don't get it. You know, the whole plot doesn't really revolve around Tyler becoming Tyler. It feels tacked on. Sure, the game wants to sell you his transitory nature as being the BIG issue of why his mother is dead, but it's pretty clear from the outset that that isn't even the case.

I think a lot of the dialogue feels forced. After 5 hours all I've done in this game is walking and talking ... or sitting and talking. It moves at a glacial pace... and right now is when it could turn out to be interesting, yet it's almost over. Trying to find out what really happened? Sure, but game needed more player agency for one and a better story flow, because the story that is there is bare bones.

I'm starting to think that Dontnod just got EXTREMELY lucky with Life is Strange. None of their other works after that comes close to it. Maybe Before the Storm ... and they didn't develop that one.
Captain Spirit was fun, because it was short and impactful, but LiS 2 already dropped the ball with overly annoying protagonists and a meandering plot with weak side characters, as well as boring gameplay. How did they manage to make the gameplay more boring than in their first attempt at this?

Tell my why stumbles into the same pit falls imho. Alyson is a blank slate with no character, while Tyler is an overly aggressive and egotistical expletive. That may of course be, because of his more unique background, but that's just the thing: Us "regular folk" will never really understand what it's like to be born in the wrong body (or feel like it, because at the end of the day we're just chemicals being passed from one point to another). It might help if Tyler were just an otherwise interesting character ... or Alyson at least. The two "can" be at odds ... and sometimes the game offers you choices that are not "black/black" or "black/white", but so far that's happened very rarely and most of the time Tyler just comes across as a total expletive.

The side characters are grey and boring as well.
There's the well-meaning "redneck" Sam, who immediately wants to shoot Tyler because of supposed trespassing and then stumbles from one "queer" pitfall into another. Give the dude a break, he's living in the backwoods and is in his 50s. He's still trying, but Tyler can only treat him like ♥♥♥♥.
We have the devout Christian "aunt", who of course wanted to put Tyler through conversion camp ... or at least suggested it. I feel like that's just another uniquely American thing, but surely that does exist. To be fair to her, that's how she's been raised and manipulated. And once again: This is a very rural place, not New York City.
In 30 years a guy like Tyler will have his own prejudices.
And of course there's the "uncle" police officer who took Alyson in after the murder, but keeps secrets.

All of the characters remain uninteresting and shallow though. You're not building a relationship with them. They're just there to put blame on at various points in the game... and always it's Tyler doing the blaming, sometimes justified, more often though not.

These protagonists have been through much, are in their early 20s (I guess) and haven't seen each other in 10 years, but now Tyler is angry that people aren't falling on their knees, begging him to let them tell him everything they remember from 10 years ago. He's an outsider ... and these people, the community, they try to move on. They're not in the right, of course, but threatening and bullying people to get them to tell you the truth is anything but mature.
But I shouldn't be surprised, because the game is wrapping its supposedly mature content in a children's book about "crafty goblins". It just feels weird and out of place. It worked in the LiS flashback episode, because Chloe and Max were actually kids then. Here it just feels awkward.

Of course I forgot Michael, who of course is also gay/bi/whatever and immediately starts hitting on Tyler the moment he sees him. That's ... weird, my man. And anything else is severe spoiler territory, but the whole enemies and allies concept is a bit irritating. They're people. Some are going to like and accept you, others won't. You can't make them like you. These things, unfortunately perhaps, need time ... and not constant in your face bombardment, as in the case of Michael, he plays no role of import whatsoever.

I remember how in LiS you had actual gameplay, you could impact the lives of others, you could learn more about others and the story still moved at a brisk pace and was packed with emotions. Or maybe I got old(er still), but I still look back fondly to that game. I spent weeks scouring forums about explanations, fan theories, etc.
I couldn't care less about any of the other characters Dontnod have come up with since ... and it doesn't help when you can't skip dialogue or scenes, especially when you're repeating them.
Max and Chloe felt more natural, their relationship developed over the course of 5 episodes and in the end they could be more than friends. Tyler and Alyson on the other hand are siblings ... and supremely irritating people. Their relationship doesn't develop, because they don't have a relationship outside their childhood memories and shared tragedies, yet they never talk about what the other one really feels or wants (because the plot needs to happen).
It just feels like Dontnod wanted a Transgender game in the style of LiS, because that's "hot" right now, but forgot to craft an actual game around it.
Uncovering actual clues about the past is kinda interesting, the rest isn't.
Maybe people from the LGBTIQ+etc. community (sorry, I can't keep up with what acronym is the politically correct one today) will find more enjoyment and representation, I can fully understand that. Personally, I just like romance in games to be an optional pursuit by the player. I'd rather have an actual plot I can follow and "solve". I doubt LiS 3 will be any better.

Some suggestions perhaps:
The game already uses this fantasy setting, why not make actual use of it? Experiencing the trauma perhaps in fantasy-like nightmare settings. At least that would break up the monotony of the game.
Get rid of mundane ♥♥♥♥ like "housekeeping" ... that's a cutscene worth 30 seconds to 1 minute at most, not a "gameplay" feature. Like so much in the game that is just filler content, because the actual story is only 30 minutes long.
Have some actually invested characters. Introduce a morality system perhaps that let's you get one someone's good/bad side. You can antagonize the whole town and your twin ... or you could try and not be a ♥♥♥♥... and maybe get some answers.
That would also make it possible to give the players more freedom in how they want to tackle the game, i.e. the overarching story is "find out why your mother did what she did" ... but it feels like you get this big info dump and at the end of the episode the whole picture changes (which surprised almost nobody)
Some actual game mechanics, less cringe-worthy dialogue, and some real stakes are needed. And you need to be able to fail!
And finally for the "power" in the game, why not let us manipulate the past? Alyson and Tyler often have conflicting memories of what happened. All you can do is pick one (and piss the other twin off .. lol). Why not "Batman" this ♥♥♥♥ and try to find out what really happened? This would of course affect the story and the ending. However it would also have required actual effort, instead of a cliché story that can only play out one way.

Salamat ミクfan
222 products in account
0
1 person found this review helpful 1

Not Recommended
11.1 hrs on record
Posted: 13 June, 2021
Sigh…I just don’t know what Dontnod is doing these days. I’m pretty thrilled Deck Nine is making the next Life is Strange as I just don’t trust Dontnod anymore. I haven’t played Twin Mirror…so maybe that’s amazing…but I doubt it. Twin Mirror supposedly takes between 6-7hrs to beat, my problem with Tell Me Why is it’s only 12hrs long. So I assume Twin Mirror suffers from the same issues this game does. The main issue is this game just doesn’t feel complete, everything about it feels half baked. This needed to be 20hrs long to develop both the ideas it’s trying to convey as well as to just develop the characters. 12hrs just isn’t enough and honestly you can probably finish this in 10hrs.

It’s a shame because I really liked a lot of the characters in this story and the setting and it’s all just wasted. It’s a very linear game. You don’t get to really explore things. The town seems really small, with the town being so small I wanted to be able to walk around and explore the town and get to know the people there and find out the small town secrets and how this tragic accident of your mothers death affected the Town. Instead you get mainly 3 places to visit: Your House, The Police Station, and the General Store. I think in total you interact with basically 5 people (Tom, Tessa, Eddy, Michael, Sam). The scope of this game is just so small.

For a Dontnod game it is also extremely linear. The main gameplay element is this idea that you and your twin can share memories and talk psychically and you can remember things differently. How you remember events basically have no impact on the story…probably because the story is so short there is no time for it to have an effect. Nor are there really any other decisions that change events in the game. Sure the ending is different depending on what your very last choice is, but that’s it. It feels like someone had this great idea of what happens if two people remember an event differently…but then never really developed that concept. The characters don’t even really disagree or really discuss the fact that they remember events differently.

Overall, the story of the game is also just very weak and doesn’t feel like the writers knew what they were doing or wanted. I think the game wanted to explore this narrative of what it would be like to be a trans individual dealing with questions of identity…but then decided people might not want to play a game solely exploring that issue so they then bolted on this mystery story…and it just doesn’t work. The reason it doesn’t work is because the mystery they created is just not interesting.

So without going into spoilers, the “mystery” of the game is the twins attempting to discover if their mother tried to murder them when they were children because she was so upset that one of them was trans or if something else was going on. This attempted murder resulted in the twins killing their mother in self defense and the trans character being sent to basically an upscale juvenile detention facility. I just didn’t care, the game I wanted would have been more along the lines of confronting people in the town over the insane injustice of bringing a criminal murder conviction against a character solely on the basis of them being trans…this issue is literally never addressed, other than a random statement that “the justice system failed them.”

The rest is going to be spoilers, but really this game fails pretty much solely on the basis of it’s story. 







It sure feels like Dontnod is great at writing characters and dialogue…but they need to focus up. Stop telling half baked stories, make longer games with more characters, more decisions that matter…don’t put out games that are short and the stories feel incomplete.

Miss_TaiPan
168 products in account
0
3 people found this review helpful 0

Not Recommended
4.6 hrs on record
Posted: 29 September, 2020
I just can't honestly, and with a straight face say that this game is good or recommend it for others. I have played DontNod's Life is Strange and I found the story (while slow initially) captivating within the first episode. The story, combined with the time travel mechanic kept me WANTING to play, guessing at what would happen next, and find new ways to explore interactions with NPCs with rewinding time. Luckily, I skipped paying money for LiS 2 as I watched a friend stream an episode and found it missed all of the magic that made the original game compelling.

Here we are again.

1. The main character so far is just kind of insufferable in some of the dialogue, and its to the point where I as a rational adult don't really have a choice in some dialogue options to not speak to people like a ♥♥♥♥ when playing as him. And just as a side note the dialogue is not as interactive as LiS. In general the game is just very linear. So linear, that the end of chapter 1 has the same "choice" presented as two different outcomes/choices.

2. There seems to be this whole "goblin" thing going with these 2 characters you play as. However, I feel that much like LiS 2 - this is just something the writers of the game's story think (emphasis on think) is some creative narrative style because much like the "two wolves" from LiS 2 - this "goblin" nonsense is just that. It doesn't seem like it will go anywhere meaningful for the player.

3. The plot hook before the end of the first chapter is just totally illogical. The entire premise is that two siblings who watched their mother chase one (the future transgender) to a dock and point a gun at them while shouting "I'm going to kill you" are now confused about if they should have killed her because they found a book about raising your transgender child. For some reason, instead of just reaching the conclusion like a sane person that she just dismissed the book's content as rubbish, or THAT SHE JUST HAD MENTAL ISSUES - the presence of this book in her room causes them to question the event. Completely contrived garbage.

4. The night their mother died is the most ridiculous portrayal of a police investigation I've seen in a "serious" game in a long time. Spoiler alert, the sister kill the mom by stabbing her in the back. She hears the mother screaming while drinking melted ice cream in the kitchen, and comes to save her sibling. Somehow, when the two kids tell the police that only the one sibling being attacked was involved and killed the mom in self defense, they didn't have any questions about why she was stabbed in the back. Or, who was drinking this ice cream spilled all over the floor in the kitchen? Who investigated this? Barney Fife?

5. Last but not least, the game is just seemingly heading for a cliff where the ending is just that the mom had mental issues. I'm assuming this before I have even reached chapter 3 because every character in the game never talks about it as a possibility even once so far. If that really is the ending/explanation then this game is even worse than I think now, and I might come back to edit this to expand on it.

Posted: 13 June, 2024
Objective interpretation, hardware report, and total game progress

Tell Me Why is a 3rd person adventure game. The game was ran on an Intel 13900k/Nvidia 4090. No system crashes noted and zero crashes to desktop occurred. One full play through was completed at 4k resolution, with max graphical settings, and steam achievement perfection was attained.

1/10 overall score and steam review template is posted below the subjective interpretation

Subjective interpretation

Well this review is certainly going to be harsh. Before I start I wish to say that my take on this game is based on the actual game itself, and not the social issue content within the game. I'm a proponent of LGBTQ+ rights generally; nevertheless, I will be focusing on the entertainment value of the game, as I do for all games. The game ran well. No bugs or crashes. The graphics were of low quality for a 2020 title. The textures on many objects appeared very muddy, and this is problematic because all you do in this game is look at stuff, ergo if everything looks horrible you're not achieving any sort of aesthetic fulfillment. Sometimes the textures are so bad that you can't read off the object you're looking at. Of course there is a feature in this game that will transfer the text of the object to a text window for you to read. I guess they perceived that this would be an issue, but they took the lazy way out and just put the text into a box. I would say the most prevalent problem of this game is its astounding lack of detail, and this present in all categories that contribute to someones recreational satisfaction. This is extremely present within the graphical realm of this game as many objects are missing parts of the models. For example barrels have no bottoms, thus if you're to look into one you would see the ground texture. The lack of detail extends to the acoustics of the title as well.

Music is very infrequent in this game, and only plays during certain cinematic parts. Nothing memorable musically, and this is disappointing, as music can server to amplify the emotional immersion of the player. This game is trying to make you feel emotion, but utterly fails at it, and this lack of musical incorporation is a missed opportunity to enhance of the quality of the game. The voice acting is flat, no emotion, and it feels like the actors are just reading off lines. Honestly, I expect a more emotive reaction from someone who's life is being threatened with a double barrel shot gun, but I guess this is too much to ask from this game. The gameplay involves you interacting with objects, and reading in order to attain information to help you solve a few puzzles. Since the appearance of the object brings me no pleasure all I am left with is reading. I could read one of the millions of books out there if I wanted to be entertained in this manner, and doing it to solve a puzzle feels like a chore. Lets talking about the story now.

The astounding lack of detail extends to the narrative of this game. The developers got small details incorrect, which further hamper the players immersion within the title. Details such as the local fauna of the environment or the appearance of a Russian orthodox church. For the fauna this game includes mentioning of skunks and raccoons being present in south east Alaska, however, these animals are not present in Alaska at all. The architecture of the Russian orthodox church is incorrect as well and appears to be more protestant in appearance. I could go on and on about the small details eroding the quality of this game, but I feel my point has being established. The sentiment that I am left with is why would I care about this story if the developers didn't seem to care about it. I feel like this game was a monetization of LGBTQ+ rights, however, it is free at the moment, but I don't recommend adding it to your library. The non giveaway price of 20$ for this game is just criminal and players should be compensated for their time playing this game instead of paying for it. This game is an absolute waste of time, and players should avoid it.

27.8 hrs on record
Posted: 10 March, 2021
S'aight...

Beautiful visuals. Good voice acting. The story is what most people play games like these for. This one's unfortunately falls short.

*Minor spoilers for all Life is Strange games*





I'll say that this game feels like it really flounders. You can tell the game is trying to channel some of what made LiS 1&2 unique. You've got the great atmospheric shots, the supernatural powers, and the stupid ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥ dead parent plot that they managed to cram into all three of the LiS games. Thing is, all three of the LiS games (four if you count Captain Spirit) managed to handle that same (sub)plot in a different way.

LiS1- You get an outsider's (Max's) point of view on the death of Chloe's dad. Instead of "feeling" the effects "directly" through the playable character, you're forced to take on a more supportive role. You may be a super-powered teenage girl, but at the end of the day, you're just trying to be there for your friend.
BTS- You get a much more intimate look at the way William's death affected a more vulnerable Chloe from a few years back, as the game is told from her point of view and before the events of LiS 1.
Captain Spirit- You explore how a child copes with the death of his mother through escapism.
LiS2- You follow a pair of siblings whose father was recently killed. They're left to fend for themselves and the game pushes their relationship to the absolute limit. How far would you *really* go for your brother?

Tell Me Why has the mystery elements of LiS 1 and the sibling bond theme of LiS 2. Other than the sloppily presented "who's the baby daddy" mystery and the weird conflicting memories mechanic (which seemed interesting at first but never really feels like it comes into play in any meaningful way), this game brings nothing new to the table. It also suffers from the same pacing problems as BTS. The whole experience just feels like a drive through the inner city. One moment you're stuck waiting around for something to happen and the next you're just speeding through everything.

Its main themes are the past and family. If you want something that's longer, better written (imo), and with more meaningful choices, play LiS 1 and 2 if you haven't already. Both of those games do those two themes better, respectively. So you have other options if you're looking for something similar. LiS 2 even has more provocative social themes, if that's what you're looking for in a game.

It's far from bad. It just falls short when you pit it against games of a similar genre. Play this if you're a big Dontnod fan or if you want to play a game with a believable trans protagonist. Or if you're just curious. It's on sale right now. First episode is free too. You might see something in it that I didn't. I ultimately would advise against getting it though.

Posted: 7 August, 2023
Tell Me Why
A promising premise hindered by poor character development and narrative beats

Note: This game was played to completion on Microsoft PC Game Pass because in this day and age, one has many avenues to play PC games (Steam, Ubisoft Connect, EA Play, Epic Games and Microsoft PC Game Pass). Stop trying to invalidatre other peoples opinions because they don't match up your criteria. Get a life and move on!

Tell Me Why is the third full length narrative-driven adventure game from studio DontNod, that same studio that hit it big with their first venture into the genre - the wildly popular and successful Life is Strange - and while much of the studios weaknesses from that game have once again carried over into this title, Tell Me Why registers as their most disappointing release yet. While I applaud the studio for picking up current day issues such as being gay or racism, bigotry and what it feels like to be a migrant in modern day America which is tackled in the first two Life is Strange games, their heavy-handidness when it comes to topics like this can often leave players at arms length.

Nuanced writing continues to evade the studio and once again poor character development is back on the menu. Tell Me Why does seem to be the most egregious of the lot though where current hot button issues such as Transgenderism and Identity Politics are so ham-fisted into the plot that you can almost hear all the woke activists cheer in loud unison. Tell Me Why introduces us to a story of family secrets and sibling bonds, except there is nothing slightly believable when it comes to the "secret" lying at the heart of this family and the sibling bond feels totally forced and faked. Not for one second did I believe that twins Tyler and Alyson Ronan actually gave two farts about each other. Their entire relationship felt like an act specifically put on for me.

Storytelling:
Just weak on all fronts. The transgender movement deserves better than what is on display here. The central focus of Tell Me Why's narrative is about exploring complex themes, such as memory, identity, sexuality and the nature of truth, but none of it is compelling or believable in the slightest. Weak plot twists, writing and character development belie the complexities of the themes being covered, making for a mostly surface level and hollow experience. While this may be their shortest game to date (at 3 episodes), the pacing is so inconsistent, with some parts dragging while other sections rush the player through important plot points that left me incredibly unsatisfied. Also the game's central mystery hinges on a plot device that is so outlandish and unbelievable that I can scarcely believe it made it into the final game at all.

Gameplay:
The gameplay mechanics in Tell Me Why follow that of the past titles and are relatively simplistic, featuring point-and-click interactions and making dialogue choices. While the focus on narrative and character-driven gameplay is understandable (as weak as it is on display here), the lack of variety in gameplay elements can feel monotonous and repetitive. More interactive elements or meaningful consequences for choices would have enhanced the overall experience.

Characters and Dialogue:
Some of the game's weakest points fall into this category, especially concerning the twins, Alyson and Tyler, who are not believable as siblings in the slightest. Their emotional journeys and the complexities of their relationship is supposed to form the heart of the game but this heart is barely on life support it feels so contrived. The dialogue is also stilted and weakly composed, failing to add any depth to either twin's personalities. Supporting characters also feel underdeveloped, leading to less impactful interactions and further emotional investment in the story .

Graphics and Art Style:
Tell Me Why features some visually appealing environments and this is probably the games strongest suit although occasional technical hiccups detract from the overall visual experience.

Audio:
The game's soundtrack is okay (once again littered with some indie music tracks), the voice acting on the other hand is sub-par which contributes to the game feeling almost like a badly written school play being poorly performed by its two leads, which you as a parent are forced to endure. Nothing in these characters voices help bring any personality to the forefront.

Length and Value:
Tell Me Why's length is relatively short and thank the gods for that, with a format of only three episodes. This may leave some players wanting more substance for their investment but not this gamer. I was just glad to see it end as this story has no believability, warmth or emotional complexity leaving behind the sour taste of disappointment.

In conclusion, Tell Me Why is a poor effort on all fronts. It fails to deliver anything compelling with shallow characters and under-developed plot twists further hindered by terrible writing. It fails to give any kind of weight to the serious themes it tackles, addressing them like one would address a store mannequin and it fails to deliver on gameplay, where there is little variety. This one is just best avoided to be honest.

One word or phrase to sum up the experience
Poor effort from a studio that continues to show diminishing returns from its games

Performance/Bug related incidents
None were experienced during my playtime with the game

Similar to games
Life is Strange, The Walking Dead - A Telltale episodic adventure, Detroit: Become Human

Rating: ★★★☆☆☆☆☆☆☆

This game is a mess. before I go in depth and spoil the story, if your even thinking of playing this, just don't. you are much better off watching a youtuber play this
