just have a good time listening to the story.

i'll start with the few (and I mean VERY few) things I actually did enjoy about this game.
firstly I think that the team did a very good job with the visuals, a lot of the backgrounds are stunning especially the mountains and other scenic views you get
in this game. The art style used for the children's book illustrations in this game are also really lovely, especially the secret loft you find nearing the end of the game.
Another thing i have to give credit to the developers on is the book of goblins, i thought it was a really neat part of the game and actually ended up reading through the
entire thing. You can tell a lot of time went into the illustrations and stories and making sure they lined up with the greater story the game was trying to tell.The puzzles
that match up with these stories are one of my favourite parts of this game as well, i thought they were really neat and would have definitely loved to see more of them. I also
do think that this game had some really emotionally compelling moments that are definitely worth seeing and Aside from all the issues i have with this game I do truly think they
had a good story to tell here, just too many problems that got in the way of making it the great game it could have been.

Those are, However, the ONLY positive things I can truly say about this lacklustre game. My first major issue with this game has to be the dialogue. So many
times while playing this game I found myself having to pause and take a moment to CRINGE from some of the absolutely TERRIBLE dialogue. Cute moments between siblings
reminiscing were fine but my problem was more with the language used in some areas, like how during a conversation between Tyler and Michael Tyler actually uses the
phrase "oh my god shut up!!" like ♥♥♥♥♥♥ teen girls do in teen Disney films like high school musical.This isn't the only issue with the voice acting for this game either,
the voice actor for Tyler gives such a poor performance it hardly seems like he feels anything at all most times unless he is angry in which he will be yelling. He's always
so monotone and delivers lines really terribly, this plays into the cringe factor of some scenes as witty banter becomes a horribly awkward moment of the player having to
stop and go "♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥ why would you say that" because Tyler's line was not delivered correctly. The game also has really terrible timing with its dialogue, so many times
did I assume a conversation was over because the characters have such a large pause between their lines. Tyler would say something to Ashley and it would take almost a whole
minute to go by before she would say her answer. Aside from Tyler though i did think that a lot of the other voice actors did a phenomenal job, Tessa had a really convincing
moment when she falls to the ground and begins crying for example. My second issue with this game is how terribly unlikable they make the main character Tyler, through the
game i had my issues with Ashley but she really stepped up near the end, accepting blame and realising some issues with herself that she needs to fix, this character
development is something we do NOT see in Tyler. Meanwhile Tyler is a self centred,self righteous, ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥ who thinks he is better than everyone around him.Tyler gets
progressively worse as the game goes on, making choices and decisions that hurt everyone around him in a sick game to make sure him being trans inst the reason for his mother
trying to kill him. Tyler shows time and time again to have zero regard for the feelings of others,literally sending his sister into a spiral where she begins hallucinating
and having panic attacks. Any of the choices you are able to make for Tyler all feel wrong and you find yourself sitting back and just yelling at Tyler alot, I found myself
getting so annoyed with him that anytime he spoke in the background scene where I was playing as Ashley I would yell at my screen telling Tyler to shut up. Hes so arrogant and
self centred,even when his sister was breaking down in front of him, crying and begging to stop digging into that terrible night Tyler KEEPS pushing her! Having one of your
main Protagonists who you are SUPPOSED TO LIKE be so terrible and just unlikable does not make for a good game at all. It made me really disconnect from him as a character
because you just can't relate with someone who is such a blatant ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥. There's no change in him by the end either to show growth, maybe the only part we see this is where
you as the player can choose to accept the police officers apology and hope the family bond will get better with time but it just feels sour because of how blatantly
ignorant Tyler has been to him this ENTIRE game, it feels fake and disingenuous how fast it switches up. I feel like this is the major reason I felt like the game just kept
going on and on and on, I didn't like one of the main characters so I didn't care about his relationships or dialogues, this made the game feel longer than it should have.
I'm not event the only person I know to feel this way, my boyfriend said the same thing and its the reason he couldn't bring himself to finish the game. Some of the visuals for
this game also aren't the best. On a regular basis characters facial expressions just did not match with what their voice or lines were implying, clothes clipping in and out,
and mouth movements not syncing up with what the character was saying.

I think the game had a very good concept and a very interesting story but it was simply executed poorly, with an unlikable main character, bad voice acting, and all in a game
that felt simply far too long it just was not a game worth anyone's time. Had this game not have been free i would NEVER have played this.
 

Neon1210
0
2 people found this review helpful 0

Not Recommended
11.3 hrs on record
Posted: 24 January, 2023
DONTNOD Entertainment have made it clear they’re done with the Life is Strange (LiS) series (which is a shame considering the limp offering Deck Nine made of Life is Strange: True Colors), but Tell Me Why is DONTNOD’s second breakaway interactive drama game that functionally acts a continuation of the LiS series without the branding. In it, we follow estranged twins, Tyler and Alyson, as they reconnect and delve into their childhood history to better understand the events that led to their separation.

Like the LiS series, Tell Me Why delivers the gameplay we’ve come to expect from DONTNOD: a people-centric story filled with more twists and turns than I’ve seen in their other entries; a charming world; mindfulness style experiential moments mixed with simple puzzles or activities; conflict-based conversations with choices to be made affecting the plot outcome. Particular praise is deserved for the inclusivity shown in the world. As a non-American without good awareness of Native American issues then I’m not best placed to comment on the indigenous peoples’ representation, but, as a gay man (who arguably also isn’t best placed to comment on transgender issues), I immediately identified with many of the interactions Tyler, a trans man, has with the town residents. There is a particular conversation with self-professed deadbeat, Sam, where he’s attempting to apologise for wrong-footing himself with Tyler earlier, and a lot of the body language and ham-handed wording is very representative of the conversations I myself have had in similar situations. Tyler does this hilariously awkward glance at one point that I know all too well, the “I get what you’re doing, but it’s honestly chill and I’d rather we just dropped it” look. And these moments of non-verbal expression are well-executed throughout the game.

Tell Me Why does a lot with a little. It’s only three chapters (compared to the usual five), utilising only a handful of environments and a similarly small cast. You go back over old environments a few times, but it never feels repetitive (something LiS: True Colors failed to do with the same idea) because it always serves something a little different. In spite of its length, the story delivers a competent mystery, and the cast is capably presented and developed, though it would’ve been nice if they’d had even more time to unfurl. I particularly enjoyed the way the twins’ attitudes to their past evolved the more they learned: Tyler moves from hatred to fascination, while Alyson goes from curious to fearful. I played LiS: True Colors not long before Tell Me Why and, for two games designing to the same length of story, Tell Me Why definitely pulls it off better.

However, despite serving a solid (though not exceptional) experience, Tell Me Why fell a bit flat for me. It’s hard to pin down exactly what made it a struggle, but my guess is the lack of driving force in the story made finding motivation to keep playing hard to come by after a break. Life is Strange 1 had the sinister threat at school, and Life is Strange 2 had the looming struggle for survival, but there’s really nothing compelling you to push Tell Me Why’s twins to continue their investigation. They could pack up their search at any point and nothing bad’ll happen other than they’ll have to make peace with not knowing more about their past (which both seem basically fine with at the beginning anyway). Furthermore, they could hypothetically come back to their research at a later point if they really wanted to. The only time sensitive element are the cast’s memories, but, given that it’s already been a decade, the key players all still seem to remember the events like they were yesterday. Consequently, I couldn’t find anything pushing me to keep going with the story. The game’s icon sat on my desktop and I kept looking past it in favour of literally anything else each time I sat down to game. And it wasn’t for lack of enjoyment, I just didn’t feel anything calling me back after a break.

Overall, Tell Me Why's a hard one to come down hard on either side of the fence. You’re probably better off just playing Life is Strange 1 or 2 over this, but if you’ve played both of those and want some more then Tell Me Why offers a short, moody trip. It never reaches the heights of its predecessors, but it’s got some nice stuff kicking about in it if you can motivate yourself in the moments where the game can’t do so itself. I don’t regret playing Tell Me Why, or even really dislike it – in fact, by the story’s crescendo in the third act, I was definitely into it – but you'll have to push to get there.

Chobi
360 products in account
1
8 people found this review helpful 1

Not Recommended
13.4 hrs on record
Posted: 2 October, 2023
If Life Is Strange, Gone Home, and The Sims had a miscarriage together, it would be this game.

(some mid-game spoilers ahead--required to support my points)

I like narrative games. I really liked Gone Home's exploration and unfolding story line. I loved Life Is Strange, it being one of my favorite games of all time. Such a picture-perfect (pun intended) combination of soundtrack, story, game mechanics, and use of time-travelling. It combined character development with an interesting plot to evoke powerful emotions in the player. Other than Max occasionally being overly campy with her internal monologue around every single classmate in the entire game (e.g., "This person likes _____. How interesting!"), it was a wonderful teenage-angst kind of thing that is almost a callback to the 80s teenage movies it often alludes to.

I played this game knowing it was going to have a lot of politics embedded in it (and it did, with the characters moaning about this or that political or activist cause every 20 minutes), but what I didn't see coming at all was the stereotypical self-centered Gen Z worldview on full display. The two main characters are objectively, legitimately...complete ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥. And yet they're supposed to be the protagonists. Everyone around them is super nice and polite...they're apologizing for merely making any little mistake every 5 minutes while the main two characters act better than everyone else and condescend to, make snide comments toward, or blame other people for everything. One character mentions seeing a type of person on TV, and they reply as if he was describing the main character--and then he apologizes later for it! But he didn't say anything wrong--he was referring to the person on TV, not the main character. This goes on over and over, from when a lady basically gave charity for months and months to their mother and then finally cut her off after she--and the main characters--started stealing from her...to when you literally find out later that they lied to the police (and more). They have crappy attitudes toward everyone for the most minor of offenses, and they are completely self-absorbed and self-centered, not caring about anyone else at all.

It just went on and on. They snidely insult Sam's desire to help someone in need as "antiquated"--of course, he genuinely cared for their mother and them, and they treat him like complete ♥♥♥♥ the entire time. These are despicable human beings. It got so bad that every time you had a binary dialog option--like many role-playing games--I would stare at the two options and think, "What do I say? The good thing that I would say, or do I role-play and say the crappy thing that these two characters would actually say?" Occasionally in these games there are bad characters where I hope that they have negative consequences (that I can make happen), but these two were so bad that I felt obligated to actually offset their terrible behavior by selecting kind, positive options in the style I usually play. So I ended up waffling a lot, sometimes selecting the jerk options because these were not good people and I either wanted to play as them or to have negative consequences for them...and then sometimes selecting the good option because I could actually stop their horrible behavior for once.

The worst part of this is the number of times they got mad at people for not committing crimes. For example, Tessa (who, like Sam, ended up apologizing despite doing nothing wrong) called CPS on the mother because she was broke and couldn't feed her kids. That's the responsible thing to do. Instead, they of course hate her for it and hate Eddy for following through with it (he has to--he's a police officer). So they want others to commit crimes for them in addition to them being criminals who lied to the police, broke into the police archives, stole from a store, and--oh yeah--killed a person.

And, to quote the great Norm Macdonald, the worst part was the hypocrisy. The main characters have a clear sociopolitical worldview, and so I can safely assume that they would insist that you call people by their preferred name. Yet they never once call their mother "Mom"--always "Mary-Ann". While there's a one-in-a-million chance she allowed them do that, it's more likely that they did that to distance themselves from her and what they did. Still, these two would likely go on a long lecture about respecting someone's preferred name and yet couldn't even call their own mother by what was likely her preferred name.

The only thing I can think of to rationalize this is that possibly this was brilliant writing regarding how off-the-deep-end the next generation is getting about thinking the world revolves around them and everyone being beneath them for not behaving in the exact way that they think they should (every interaction between the main characters and anyone else reminded me of the Twilight Zone episode, The Good Life, where everyone had to act exactly how the kid wanted or he'd wish them out into the corn field). Alyson gets offended at Sam calling her "princess" when that's literally the word the mother used for herself throughout the entire game. These characters had their heads so far up their rectal cavities that I'm one of the 0% out of 100% that went with Tom's view of events at the end because I assumed that they were probably being biased and stupid like they were the whole game.

There were some great moments that saved this from being a total slog, like the amazing finale where you complete puzzles and learn about the mother's history. That was amazing, and I liked the mother because she was a real, 3-dimensional character that you could empathize with. She was far from a perfect person, but she had more redeeming qualities and character in a few flashbacks and puzzles than the two main characters had the whole game. The graphics were great and the scenes were beautiful. But between the main characters being insufferable and the game being excruciatingly slow (at one point, you watch a pillow in slow motion for a full 10 seconds), I couldn't recommend anyone sit through it to get to those few beautiful moments. I mentioned "The Sims" at the beginning of this review because literally all you do is the most monotonous stuff like get the house ready to move and do inventory at the store. How did they think that these activities would make for a good game? No idea. There are also a lot of mistakes in the game, such as the use of the metric system where the imperial one would've been used and the people wearing clothing outside that was way too light given the snow everywhere (they repeatedly say it's freezing outside, but one of the characters never wears a hat or a winter coat).

I was hoping to be proven wrong about this game and thought that short reviews saying that the main characters were unlikable were overblown, but they were underblown. In the same vein that the characters kept wishing for terrible things like their house burning down and such, I had wished this was like Life Is Strange meets The Butterfly Effect and you could go back and stop these two characters from being born because all but one of the other nice, good, responsible characters deserved to have nice lives free from these jerks who hate, insult, and look down on them the whole time. Eddy did the right thing (as a police officer). Sam did the right thing (being a helpful, caring person). Tessa did the right thing (in being charitable until she was stolen from). The fact that the creators of this game thought that self-centered, self-righteous characters would make for good protagonists--and that this got so many good reviews (possibly by people with similar attitudes)--concerns me for the future of humankind if this is how the majority of society will act one day and see no ethical problems with it.

16.3 hrs on record
Posted: 29 June, 2022
I like the lgbtq+ representation, and it was cool that the game was completely free in June. However, the characters felt very flat. Without getting into specifics for those who haven't played the game, the puzzles are cool and fun to solve, but the actual story has a ton of leaps in logic that are very strange. The siblings come to conclusions using evidence that isn't really there. When you do have evidence or bits of memory, it's usually underwhelming and doesn't really add a whole lot to the story. The fairy-tale story aspect is a very cool idea, but it could be better executed. The powers of the siblings seems like it was put in the game just to give it a Life-is-Strange-element to it. The actual power doesn't really add a whole lot, except that you can visually see memories of the siblings. However, like I said before, the memories do not really add much to the evidence of the story, the development of the characters, or the progression of the events. They seem like they are very much just placed in there to make the game longer. The other characters that the siblings interact with are interesting, and I like how they correlate to the storybook aspect of the game. However, even they seem a little flat and very unrealistic in how they react at certain points of the game.

Visually, the graphics are really well done, and I like the character designs and the style of everything. It feels a lot like Life is Strange in that way. However, the characters feel a little surreal in their movements, sometimes they move very life-like and other times they only move their mouths when speaking. This can be very unnerving when talking to NPCs. Especially in the cut scenes where you can move the camera, the characters seem very puppeted. Some of the scenes in which the siblings are walking and talking together are pretty, but it feels like all the attention is on the landscape of the game (which is beautiful, don't get me wrong) and not on the story or the individual movements of the characters. The conversations with some of the other characters are interesting (I like Micheal and his interactions with Tyler lol) but a lot of them seem pointless, like they are just there to add filler. Not a lot of the actual choices in the game seem to matter, and even they are few and far in between.

Overall, I think it's a cool concept, and I think it could be a cool game, but it's trying to be Life is Strange and not really focusing on what it does have going for it (the fairytale story aspect and the different characters). If the whole game wasn't a big mystery that isn't all that huge then I think it could be really good.

I don't know if I recommend this game. I think it's worth it for the bit of representation and the beautiful graphics, not so much for the actual story or the choices-aspect. 6/10

Really falls short, coming from LiS 1&2.

The story is extremely slow paced, even for a storytelling game. I went into it knowing each chapter is anywhere from 3-5 hours long, and after 2 hours that only discouraged me further.

Yes, I think it's admirable that they're trying to educate people about the challenges of being transgender. No, I don't think treating the player and other characters within the story as ignorant troglodytes, aggressively and condescendingly is the right way to do it. Calling a man "Antiquated" for trying to lend a hand to a single mother with twins?
If he had just turned a blind eye to her struggles, then they would've complained about that, too. Make up your minds. $50 that at least one of your screenwriters has neon pink hair.

You've introduced a lot of other controversial topics into your games. We already expect it. They add flavor, stakes, and emotional investment to them. This, however, is an actual detriment to the story you're trying to tell.

I'm still looking forward to LiS 3. Tell your story. I felt infuriated on Sean and Daniel's behalf on 2 when they'd get discriminated. That's the feeling you want to achieve. Frustration after the 500th time something about the LGTVOLED+ community is mentioned? That's a no-no. You're not educating and spreading love. You're teaching more people to hate.

To end this in a positive note, the character models and general layout of the scenes was great. It made me want to keep playing, if only to keep sightseeing for a little longer.

Unlike an logical comprehensive storyline that fits together well and keeps you immersed and empathatic towards the protagonist like in LiS or LiS:BTS the story gets divided by puzzles. N o i r
0
3 people found this review helpful 0

Not Recommended
3.1 hrs on record
Posted: 20 February, 2024
Product received for free

Dontnod used to be one of my favorite game developers. They made the Life is Strange games, the first of which is one of my favorite games of all time. However, this seems to take a detour from their usual quality standards. I cannot speak to the quality of the entire story, because I could only make it through the beginning before I got too bored to go on. The game has that same classic Dontnod feel both in terms of visuals and controls, but the story is just not great. Dontnod has a history of tackling important societal issues in each game, which is good, and that remains true here, but that seems to be the entirety of this story. It feels more like a love letter to certain topics rather than an actual game. Another problem is that the characters are just not relatable. While the aspect of gender identity can be relatable to some, just going by how the characters in the story act, it's hard to understand them. After playing three hours of the game I still know very little about the story of the twins, apart from what was divulged in the opening exposition of the game. Additionally, the twins are both just not nice to each other. I get that sibling rivalry exists but it seems that every other line of dialogue between the two comes off as a jab to one and other or a backhanded compliment. It's hard to become invested in these characters and care about them when, from what you see in the first three hours at least, they just aren't nice people. I wish I could recommend this game, but I can't. This is an odd left hook to Dontnod's usual work and it seems that their quality is beginning to go downhill, just like so many other companies. It's truly sad to see. I was fortunate enough to pick this game up for free during a sale, but if you are considering spending money on this, just don't.

After finishing the game I was extremely disappointed even though 1) it was a freebie and 2) I didn't expect much in the first place.

You get through the slogfest (which was named here Episode 1) with weird camera angles and unnatural dialogue, then Ep. 2 starts and it feels far better, but the dialogue part of the game still often looks like it was ripped straight out of bad fanfiction. You think 'ok I can do that, I can finish the game for the sake of the story' but it's dragging and dragging and there's a whole lot of rubbish info and options and scenes and characters that do not contribute to the whole premise at all unlike it was in LiS. Then Ep. 3 starts and you pretty much hyped to learn the truth already but turns out the whole story buildup doesn't make any sense in the end and you've been suffering for nothing. I'd be far more satisfied If I'd just looked up starting cutscene of the game and endings on YT, because that's how the whole story looks like laid bare. Everything in between is just a filler.

Also what irks me is that 2nd protagonist, Tyler, is very unlikable character and the game seems to push his narrative with 'bond' mechanic making him even more unlikable since said mechanic doesn't make sense. There are two types of decisions in the game: the one which drives siblings away from each other and the one that tightens their bond. But quite often decisions deemed by the game as 1st type have literally nothing to do with it. It mostly happens when you take Aly's position instead of Tyler's and it's not like you're choosing between them separating or them being together, you're choosing between their different opinions on situations or between their different memories. That's it. It doesn't contribute to their relationship in the aforementioned matter, only that somehow it does and If you don't agree with Tyler's vision you're driving the twins apart.

That being said, it's not entirely a terrible game, it has its moments, but you won't miss anything If you won't try it.

ragingfire
0
8 people found this review helpful 1

Not Recommended
9.0 hrs on record
Posted: 2 December, 2020
I cannot recommend this game to anyone. It has the original Life is Strange 'Vibe'. But thats all it is. After playing it, I see it only played upon my nostalgia of Arcadia Bay and offered no subtance of its own.

You play as a transgender character which is unique, if you come from a certain political perspective you will find this game connects to you very well. In its defense I can say they did not take it as far as the could have, as far as for example Life is Strange 2 did take it.
So if you are doubtfull of enjoying a game with a prescribed point of view you have to ask yourself if this story if for you to begin with.

The gameplay is a strange mix of little busiwork, tiny puzzles and button prompts. It cannot be overstated how bad it is. If you place it side by side with other games in its genre you might see similarities. But you have to realise that "picking up the trash" in a narrative driven game is only exciting gameplay if you are either: Still contemplating on wtf just happened to your character or super scared of what might just happen next. the spell of the storyline is so easily broken that most of the time you spend uninterested and just clicking through the gameplay.

The story is a crime mystery, supernatural experience, tale of two sisters and a transsexual transition all in one. It is all over the place. It shifts incredibly fast from one to the other, and leaves you out of the loop and in total disbelief of the protagonists and their reactions. Or of those of the people around them. This makes you disconnect with everything that is happening. (Alysson can tell Eddy a certain something, and then walk out the door within 20 seconds without it having any effect on the story)

The setting of Alaska, its locations are beautiful, like i said in the beginning, this game does have the Life is Strange vibe. It will enchant you for a bit but theres just nothing there to hold ur attention for 9 hours.

Yeast Lord
0
1 person found this review helpful 0

Not Recommended
11.3 hrs on record
Posted: 21 March, 2021
Made from the guts of the Life is Strange storytelling and a gentle touch of sci-fi thriller. It failed to impress as much as its older counter parts.

While the scenery and characters felt more alive, The narration of the story was the thorn in my side. The plot was good, but the squeeze of their personalities aggravated me.

Understanding that you MUST portray those characters, as they choose their role for you, irritated me in a game about choices.

Spoilers ahead:

1. To gay or not to gay.
If I am forced to play as a trans male, why must I be obligated to choose between gay or to abstain? Why does this matter? Why not trans-male-lesbian? More importantly, why force-feed that into the story when it didn't advance the plot at all? Because of this, I could not relate to the character at all. Although, I am grateful that a character like this exists for those who needed it. But trying to walk a mile in their shoes and all, is good, but was a hard pill to swallow because I didn't like them. >inb4 homophobic comments.

2. What are plot elements?
I liked the metaphor from the stories, but you don't find the 'A-ha!' moment in the story because its literally a collection of stories you get in the beginning and constantly use to solve the puzzles. So... what is the climax, if the book told you who the baddy was all along? Choosing who to blame the guilt on. No, really.

3. Limited choices.
Throughout the LiS series, you had to make many choices that mattered or vastly changed how the story arc was. It was emotionally charged and went as the player's emotions did. However, in TMW, you have to choose to side angsty man-baby or scared girl. There was never a middle ground where you can choose to keep a cool head and investigate further.

4. Too cafe-house, not enough indie.
The main draw a player comes to a Dontnod game is how they bring raw emotion and captivation to their story telling. In LiS: How many times did you want to hug Kate and tell her she was gonna be okay? "Okay great, now... Do that, but with whatserface, because we told you to." The problem was the character's defining moments were one-shots instead of building up to a relationship. When Aly had her confession/breakdown, nothing built up to it. It just happened by deciding to push a button. But in LiS, from the moment you talked to Kate, and saw her several times after, to the time she was about to jump, you built that emotional tie to her. That frantic heart wrenching moment when your actions determined if she would live or die was powerful, and sorely missed here.

In conclusion:

If you are a gay trans-male, you like murder-mystery, and simple game mechanics focused on narrative, give the first episode a try, you might get hooked and enjoy it.

If you like substantial emotional stories that focus on player choice, and fulfilling story arcs that blow your mind. Try elsewhere. I should have.

18.6 hrs on record
Posted: 6 August, 2021
Product received for free

What's sad about Tell Me Why, it's that deep inside this game has a great and good story, but it's buried underneath a big pile of poorly written dialogue, unnecessary forced agenda and soulless characters. And what makes it even sadder is that the game overall looks stunning; it’s beautiful, the graphics are amazing and the exploring is enjoyable.

I was truly interested in the twins' past, in their evolution and how the really coped with all the trauma. About how their mother influenced their character, about the whole “memory” mechanics and how the twins were bound together. This entire back story hooked me, it was good and I wanted to give a resolve to their story (I am referring about the endings, but I will not spoil them). So why I am saying “back story”? Because all the LGBT scenes (which this game so hardly tried to impersonate) are really empty and they feel forced and entirely detached from reality, as if the devs made a small research on the internet and chose to represent what they think about this matter and not illustrating the experience as it should be.

Tyler IS a very interesting character (it is even more likeable than his sister) but every time he pointed out obsessively about his gender, managed to take me out of the story I was enjoying and from the immersion. I was expecting a good LGBT story, but it is so poorly written that if you remove every interaction/mention about Tylor being trans, the story itself is not changing. It does not add anything good to the entire plot and it can be literally cut out without impacting how the story evolves. That bad.

Skaava
0
1 person found this review helpful 0

Not Recommended
11.5 hrs on record
Posted: 2 July, 2023
I enjoyed Tell Me Why, but wouldn't recommend playing it. Instead, I'd say buy a copy and then try and watch someone on YouTube who doesn't narrate as they play just take you through it (hopefully cutting some of the least important story elements out along the way).

Allow me to explain.

Tell Me Why starts off STRONG.... There's very much a 'This is going to be ten times better than the meandering, whiny, and claustrophobic 'Life is Strange: True Colors'. You get a feel you might be getting into what should have been Life Is Strange 3.... Right off at the start, you're shown this vast ocean scene with a rich field of view, and you have a sense you will be able to explore a story in a large sandbox with great characters. That sense of freedom gets expanded upon outside of a gas-station / mini-mart. You get the feeling the world will be opening up.

That... ends up not being the case, but the story at least keeps you interested for the remainder of the episodes. In fact, what ends up happening is you have a good story hidden behind a mechanically and interactively weak game. Tell Me Why would've been better off as a movie than a game, and the few times it feels like it's trying to be a game (fishing, backroom tag, a file investigation that's barely a game, and a few puzzles that feel like old NES educational video game challenges more than actual games), it just feels... bad.

The Dontnod team maintains their excellent story telling track record but ruins it by cutting a lot of corners. The one good thing about Tell Me Why is that some of the story moves along fast enough that you don't have time to notice how small the game is compared to any of the three Life is Strange entries. Unfortunately, they take a good story with decent pacing and instead of making it feel truly interactive or deciding 'lets just make an FMV project', they tried to force it into a Life-is-Strange shaped box that didn't feel right for this project.

Finally, when you do reach the end, there are just too many dangling threads - they keep the focus on the kids and maybe because it's the kids story, that was an intentional choice. Still though, when you do character driven, it would be nice to see how everyone ends up, not just your two main characters.

So again - Don't waste your time playing it, but don't be afraid to find a way to watch a highly edited version of it so it feels more like a tv mini-series. Maybe if they see enough people paying for it on steam but having 0 hours of playtime, they'll get the message and go back to the drawing board for their next project?

Not Sure
0
1 person found this review helpful
1 person found this review funny 0

Not Recommended
10.5 hrs on record
Posted: 10 July, 2023
When I first saw this game, I was excited to play it. It seemed like it would be a very emotional story about abuse and gender identity, which are topics that people can find relatable and easy to sympathize with. However, upon playing the game I quickly came to the realization about the writing and dialogue. Everything is over-narrated and the two main characters are cringey and unlikable, especially Tyler. To put it bluntly, Alyson is an idiot and Tyler is a prick. Tyler is so quick to be defensive and rude to everyone for the smallest things that are not even remotely their fault, and the fact that they even try to be nice to Tyler makes them genuine heroes. The story overall is just a complete mess because the way it is presented by the game is constantly throwing new questions at the player and having them go on a wild goose chase to the point where some parts of the game seem genuinely pointless. The story tries so hard to blame side characters, such as Eddie and Tom even though they basically did nothing wrong. To summarize without spoiling the story, Tyler gets mad at Eddie for being a police officer that does his job, and both Tyler and Alyson get mad at Tom for regretting a mistake he made like 20 years before the events of the game. At the end of the game it surprises the player with a plot twist that has no build up or realistic foundation whatsoever, and tries to make one of the most humble and likable characters into the bad guy, and yet still fails to do so. In fact at the end of the game I was more against Tyler and Alyson than at the beginning, because by trying to put the blame onto someone else, it somehow just made the main characters seem even more like ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥. Every side character, even the extremely minor side characters like an old man you talk to once at the very beginning of the game, are really likable or at least have some redeeming qualities. The main characters might actually be the worst written main characters I have seen in a videogame ever, because it tries so hard to convince the player that they are good people, but fail miserably because they act like total incompetent ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥ throughout the entire story. The best part of the game was in the third chapter, when Alyson was having a panic attack and crying, and I can't tell if that part was good because it's easy to sympathize with someone who is having a panic attack, or because it was the only part of the game where the main characters shut the ♥♥♥♥ up. It honestly frustrates me that I have to dislike this game so much because it takes on topics that some can find relatable and very serious and emotional, and it frustrates me even more that most of the people who played this game liked it as much as they did. People only like this game because it talks about abuse, gender identity, and it was free during pride month. Not even the gameplay is good. The puzzles are just reading a line of text and pressing a button that lines up with the text, which is literally what teenagers have to do as homework for their history class. The dialogue is poorly written and the voice acting is mediocre, and having conversations in the game is the equivalent to seeing a choice of two dialogue options that feel like picking between the good ending or the bad ending, because it is so mind numbingly simple. The worst part is that no matter what, the main characters still end up as ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥ that didn't learn a thing even if you get the "good" ending.

TLDR: The dialogue and writing sucks, the gameplay sucks, the story is a cluster ♥♥♥♥, the main characters are extremely unlikable, and this game got the opposite of review bombed because there's a trans person in it.

1/10 the only good part was that it's free during pride month.

Not Recommended
8.7 hrs on record
Posted: 23 June, 2021
Product received for free

Although I enjoyed parts of the game and appreciate getting this for free during Pride Month, I can't recommend it as a title you'd have to pay for. A lot of negative reviews state the game "pushes an agenda" or is "political". That is just plain stupid as neither are true. As for my own thoughts:

The story itself is extremely shallow and padded over too many hours. It can be summarised in a few minutes using the beginning of episode 1, the middle of 2, and the end of 3. Most of the conversations are outright boring and don't contribute much to the plot. The characters are uninteresting, and the biggest driver behind the plot is how the two protagonists remember things from their childhood. The endings of the game are based on which of the twins' memory you choose to canonise. It's only two extremes, A or B, with no middle ground.

In the first chapter, which almost caused me to stop playing altogether and would've prompted me to request a refund if I had actually paid for it, Tyler's character is extremely unlikeable. I'm all for trans representation in video games, but I don't think the way it was implemented is a good way to go. His gender identity is his only personality for the majority of the game aside from being an utter jerk to everyone around him in the first chapter. This clears up during the game, but the character remains shallow and neither show a lot of growth during the three episodes.

I did finish the game over the course of a few nights in the hope that it would lead to some satisfying ending, but this never happened. I can recommend giving it a go now that it's free, but otherwise I'd stay clear. DontNod have some very decent titles out there but this isn't one of them.

killerkaetzchen

1 person found this review helpful 0

Not Recommended
21.3 hrs on record
Posted: 21 September, 2022
Product received for free

Less of a game and more of a high-quality 3D visual novel.

Pros:
- good graphics
- interesting storyline dealing with various themes such as trauma and memory, LGBT issues, family reunions, digging up the past etc.
- generally well-voiced
- chapter/scene shortcuts to obtain collectibles and replay specific events is very nice to have.

Cons:
- not that much to do - each scene really only has a couple of key items/people you need to interact with to progress.
- actions and walking around feel very sluggish, especially the memory sections.
- not that many different scenes, you'll be in locations multiple times.
- replaying to get different outcomes is kinda tedious, even with the conversation skip mechanic, so I recommend a speedhack here.

I got this game for free so I really can't complain too much, but I don't think I'd buy it if I had to.

patily095

Not Recommended
19.2 hrs on record
Posted: 17 July, 2024
I recently played " Life is Strange " by DONT NOD which was followed by the second one, Life is Strange: Before the Storm developed by Deck Nine.

The first Life is Strange had me at first with its setting, Max, its main character, her day-to-day struggles (but also, growing up story) living as a teenage girl becoming a young woman / art student, I was enjoying the story, that was for more than half of the game, until... the later part became , which was not done well in my opinion, and felt very sloppy and cheap.
And Max’s superpowers which were never really explained nor made any sense (not even in a fantasy setting) would change logic out of nowhere almost as an excuse to move the story in different directions.
This was not a " plot twist " but more like a lazy writing mechanic.

I did like the main characters, Max and Chloe but in the end, I didn't like the story.

A very different thing was the second game "Before the Storm" which was done by Deck Nine. You can check my review for that game for the details, but basically the game took the same characters but with excellent writing and the story elevated itself to unexpected heights. The main character in the game Chloe Price and her relationship with Rachel Amber was written in a way that felt more raw and sincere and didn't shy away from showing a heartfelt love story between two teenage girls. Even if that game was just a secondary story to the first one, it felt so much more meaningful and emotional.


Tell me why is the second game I play from Dont Nod, and sadly I see the same problems I saw in the first Life is Strange. (still have to play the third and fourth ones)

Tyler and Alyson are the two main characters of this story… It seems to be about them, at first, about their childhood being twin sisters one of them being queer and the other loving him no matter what.

The story soon devolves into one of the secondary characters struggles, and so, Tyler as well as Alyson are practically relegated to the back, just being spectators (the same as us, the players) in everything that happens because the game soon devolves in just a long road through memories understanding the past of another character.


Now, this could be perhaps a misunderstanding on my part, but I was under the impression that the game started as one story and ended up as another.

The narrative was always from the brothers point of view, yes, but it was really about someone else.

Maybe because of that, or just how the story was written, the main "story" itself about this other character to me always felt bland and uninspired. It had a thing or two to " reveal " at the end to the brothers but it was too little, too late.

One of the two twins, Tyler being transexual, wasn't really something that was featured prominently. The game kind of markets itself at times as being " LGBTQ+" friendly and it even has a loading screen reminding you that they consulted with GLAAD about trans representation and also telling you that you can seek help if needed.

It is a double edge sword I believe... because it certainly fills my heart to play a game with a trans main character since I love to play as a woman or trans or any other character besides your middle age/young man. But, trying to lean too much on it without being that much important, seems to be a disconnected narrative, putting the " label " to it to something that really isn't.

Also, the trans character having “a tragic past” and being afraid of being himself because of how difficult it was being trans, while it is something realistic it’s also becoming something tiring and repetitive to see really quick.

As a trans person myself while I value the struggles of being Trans shown on media, I would also like to see Trans people just being themselves, doing any other thing (other than being sad) having a relationship, being happy, being sad, being funny, being a good person, being a bad person, just being, a person like anybody else. And not be pathologized and put in a “box “because of being “trans“. That’s like assuming any gay person needs “help“ because they’re gay.

I think that way of looking at trans people has to change.

And, to be clear, this is not a complain about the story in Tell me why being " not trans enough " but more about appearing to be going one way but then going another way.
If the story is not really about Tyler being trans, and more about this other character, it is completely fine, but then it should be more focused on what it really is.

This is more a family drama; two twins have a traumatic family tragedy when they were young... they reunite later in life as young adults to take care of the family house and so they investigate what really happened.... oh, and one of them happens to be trans.
If you want to play a game with a story centered on at least one aspect of being Trans I recommend “If found “a small game by dreamfeel which feels much stronger on what it wants to say to you and doesn’t hold anything back from telling you an honest story from an honest point of view.
In Tell me why, it is important for Tyler’s character to be trans, absolutely. It defines much of him as a character. But the story is not really about Tyler, is about .

So, in the end the message is mixed, it dilutes as it happens, and while the game is beautifully done, with some great visuals, some good music and nice voice acting, as usual by DONT NOD, the story falls.

This review written ©2024 by Aleena.

Not Recommended
0.2 hrs on record
Posted: 12 January
Uninspired and Underwhelming

Tell Me Why sets out to tell a deeply personal story with important themes, but unfortunately, it struggles to deliver on its potential. While it has moments of emotional resonance, the weak pacing, lack of meaningful player agency, and repetitive gameplay make it a disappointing experience.

The story is the heart of the game, but it fails to leave a lasting impression. While the relationship between the twins, Tyler and Alyson, is central to the narrative, their dynamic feels underexplored. The game often relies on surface-level dialogue and flashbacks instead of giving the player deeper moments to connect with the characters. The mystery surrounding their past starts off intriguing but fizzles out as it becomes predictable and heavy-handed. By the time the major revelations unfold, they lack the emotional impact the game clearly intended.

The gameplay, much like other Dontnod titles, revolves around exploration and dialogue choices, but here it feels especially limited and repetitive. You spend much of your time walking through small environments, interacting with objects, and piecing together memories. While this sounds engaging in theory, the execution is underwhelming. The exploration feels like busywork, with most interactions offering little to no meaningful context. The memory mechanic, which allows you to see conflicting versions of the past, is an interesting idea but ultimately feels underutilized and gimmicky.

Another major disappointment is the lack of player agency. While the game presents itself as a narrative-driven adventure with choices that matter, most decisions feel inconsequential. The outcomes barely change the story, leaving you with the impression that your input doesn’t really matter. It’s frustrating to feel like a passenger in a game that’s supposed to be about shaping a personal, emotional journey.

The pacing is also an issue. The game drags through its three episodes, with long stretches where very little happens. While Dontnod is known for slow-burn storytelling, Tell Me Why takes this to an extreme, often feeling like it’s padded with unnecessary filler. This, combined with the game’s small, lifeless environments, makes the experience feel tedious and uninspired.

On a positive note, Tell Me Why deserves credit for its representation of underrepresented communities. Tyler’s portrayal as a transgender man is respectful and groundbreaking, and the game does well to handle this aspect with care. However, representation alone doesn’t make up for a weak story and bland gameplay.

In the end, Tell Me Why feels like it’s trying to replicate the emotional depth of games like Life is Strange but lacks the nuance, charm, and impactful storytelling that made those games stand out. While it’s worth acknowledging the game’s intentions, the overall execution leaves much to be desired.

I'm going to list the positive things first:
The setting is very unique (set in Alaska) and the character setup is also unique, getting to play as 2 different twins and one of them is trans. The sound is also really good and plenty of immersive outdoor sounds, etc.

Now onto the bad..
The game is rather long, it took me 21 hours to beat as more or less a completionist and there are only 3 chapters. The story is there but it's spread thin over the 21 hours and a lack of characters. I get it, it's a small town in Alaska, but come on. After the second chapter I debated on even finishing the game as it was getting boring and I was losing interest in some of the characters and the story. There aren't a lot of characters and there's only 1 romance option who is a gay man. Better than nothing but I was hoping for 2 or 3 different options. There wasn't a lot of music in the game unlike Life is Strange. It tried to focus on a touchy piano score which somewhat worked. Overall it was no where near as fun, interesting or exciting as Life is Strange. I kept thinking it would get more and more exciting but it was rather the opposite and they teased this bear attack and I really believed they would do a scene with it and it never happened! (would have added a lot if it did). Things like that would have made this a much more exciting game and I feel that it missed out on a lot of opportunities. Everyone is a little too nice, even if they are an antagonist. The gameplay felt very simple and I was really hoping for more here.

This game is actually very well done, story wise. It explores some challenging themes and I really enjoyed it. The game play was pretty good too - I didn't feel like any of the puzzles were too challenging but I still felt a sense of achievement when I cracked them. The artwork is gorgeous and I love the main characters.

You're probably wondering why I don't actually recommend this game, then, if I've just talked about how I really liked it. What I wouldn't recommend is buying this game at full price - if you can get it for free or heavily discounted, then do it. This game was so hard to actually get to run, it got to the point that I had to play it at low graphics on my AMD laptop because it wouldn't run on my Intel gaming PC. If you look at the community hub for this game as well you'll see the bug reports are several comments long and there hasn't been any follow up from the developers in a very long time. This game seems to have been abandoned, basically. It's a real shame because it is amazing but so many people can't play it or progress in the story because of several problems that should be solved by now. I was lucky I had another computer that actually could play it - a lot of people don't have that option.

In short, the story itself is amazing and the game play is pretty good. I still do not recommend it because of the difficulty I had actually getting it to run. It's current year. This should not be an issue. Don't buy this at full price.

ThatDudeNika

No one has rated this review as helpful yet 0

Not Recommended
12.8 hrs on record
Posted: 16 September, 2020
This is more of a visual novel than an interactive game, but what it does it does supremely well.

It tells the story of two siblings reunited after a whole lot of years, trying to sort out some things before selling off their family home. As with all of Dontnod's games there is a supernatural element in this, too. They can share thoughts and can see memories play out before them and even discuss them since both see it.

Visually I think it uses the same engine even Life Is Strange 1 used, but the texture quality is great so it doesn't look too dated. Sound design is amazing, with nice songs in the background and phenomenal voicework on the main characters in particular.

As for the story or the core gameplay... ouff. This is where the game just falls apart. Sadly I have to revise my originally-positive review. While the game sets itself up great and the chemistry between the two leads is enjoyable, the extreme underuse of the main feature coupled with very flat and mostly automated puzzles just makes for a rather shallow game. By the end I was glad it was over as it was just ... boring, really. The thing is, if they had simply allowed the memory feature to be used ~always, akin to the rewind in LiS1, I think it could have been truly great.

The way it is, it's worth it on a deep sale, but nothing else.

i would recommend this only if you're interested in trans representation in a video game narrative. otherwise, go play life is strange instead.

Not Recommended
1.8 hrs on record
Posted: 31 July, 2022
Positives:
- The scenery is wonderful
- The details are stunning, for example drawings in the childhood book, items are well designed
- Physics of the game are mostly good

Negatives:

- The transgender bit is a bit too much cliche and the story takes almost a comic turn when all of a sudden all these random transgender themes are being discussed and forced upon the player

- Interaction with objects is horrible, the player model has to be coming from a specific angle and stand still in a very specific position just to be able to grab a item from a table which also makes the game a pain in the ass to play

- The difficulty is weird and jumps from absolutely obvious things which can be solved in a split second to riddles which make no sense even when solved and can take several minutes of guessing which slows down the game

Overall it was a decent game, especially if you grabbed it for free there is no damage in playing it, but I would never pay for this game, and would be much more demanding if I did so. It was fun goofing around for a few hours with friends while playing it but it is definitely nowhere near the best story based games you could get like Until Dawn, Last of us, etc...
 

S.
48 products in account
0
8 people found this review helpful 1

Not Recommended
14.2 hrs on record
Posted: 17 August, 2024
Product received for free

Tell Me Why... No seriously... Tell Me...

I'm probably about to upset an entire fanbase, but I'm going to be honest. Tell me why sucks..
This "game" tells the story of two twins who share memories with a "mysterious" past, that only happened ten years ago, which they seem to be covering up. Yeah who doesn't remember their mom trying to shotgun your brother, only to kill your own mother by stabbing her in the back with a pair of scissors, and then lying to the cops about it. Who wouldn't remember that?

But as players of the game you learn about this in a very unnatural way, especially because you are playing as the two characters. Oh hey we have twin powers and we can communicate without talking to each other "Hey do you remember this?", "Oh I remember it differently", choose which memory we are going to use. Frankly I couldn't give less of a crap because these are very vanilla characters, hiding under a "woke" mystique. "Oh Tyler use to be a little girl, and they transitioned and now they go by Tyler." so it feels like they are just hiding behind this cloak to get good reviews, because it would be wrong and bigoted of you to hate on a game with LGBTQ representation. Because everyone is so scared of saying something that will "offend" the snowflakes of this generation. Well I'm sorry honesty is the best policy and slapping the woke bumper sticker on this just so people won't call your game bad is cheap.

My issue with Tyler is not that he/she/it is a trans character, my issue with Tyler is that there is ZERO charisma and nothing that actually makes for a good character. The same can be said for Alison the other twin. I don't see a "mystery" in a game where the characters have ALL of the pieces, and then pretends to lose them. Not a great excuse for going around town harassing everyone. Your mother who you refer to as "Mary-Ann" which is extremely awkward, chases Tyler with a shotgun and gets stabbed with scissors, ten years ago, I'm afraid I don't need to know anymore about this. I fell asleep more than once over how bland and uninteresting the story is.

At least with Life is Strange you had the "rewind" mechanic, fighting against the clock. "What are we gonna do, the world is falling apart but I have to save my best friend from getting killed." so you rewind time to save your best friend, causing reality to collapse around you. Which is a interesting concept, unlike oh I don't know, NOT REMEMBERING WHEN YOU KILLED YOUR MOTHER TEN YEARS AGO. So now all you basically do is fall asleep and spam interact with the scripted scenes.

So the main reason I completed the game was for achievements, and the plot takes a nosedive from chapter one, not that I thought it could get any worse. The LGBTQ is so apparent and in your face, every building you step into has LGBTQ representation and there are maybe ten characters of importance where half of them fall into this category "Oh Jack that is such an anti-gay thing to say!" to which I say, they are used as PROPS. They are there to tell you that you should be worried about telling everyone around that you are trans because it would take a "lifetime" to "educate" them. It's so dismissive, and it seems to be part of the "liberal agenda" that shines through in Tell Me Why. You have to be out and proud, and tell everybody constantly. Everyone is fighting their own battle, no one cares.

The game also didn't really offer that much variety in terms of gameplay, some mini games like catching fish, or how you are too stressed so use your de-stress app thing. Honestly my favourite part about Tell Me Why is the book of goblins. Its a book Mary-Ann wrote to teach her kids valuable lessons through stories in a cryptic fashion. The stories are interesting and helps with the overall world building, unfortunately this is not why you play a game. The story book would have a much greater use in the story book realm, you use it to figure out puzzles, of which there are just a few. That might be the biggest part that you can actually call a game here.

Oh but wait... The ending is a total poopooshow. So throughout the game Alison and Tyler prove to be unreliable narrators, they remember events differently and its up to the player to decide which memory is going to be your "truth". The final choice is between Alison choosing to believe Tyler when he said their mom was going to kill him or choosing that he is misremembering the event before stabbing her in the back with scissors. This is the final nail in the coffin of Tell Me Why, giving the player this false idea that choosing what to remember and what happened will somehow change the outcome. Given the fact that the twins already figured out that their mother had already confronted a guy at the docks with a threat to shoot him, and they are just conflating the memories. The reality is Mary-Ann was then ostracised by the community. With Mary-Ann dead it's easy for the townspeople to twist the narrative, and thats the good ending. You are supposed to believe what people told you and build a false narrative to protect yourself, so you can live happily in the present. If 1+2=3 but everyone says its 4, then you have to believe its 4 right?

This game goes so far off the woke deep end, it is frightening. If this is what people consider as good storytelling these days I have no hope for the future of gaming. I give tell me why a 3 out of 10. Get it on sale or let someone else waste their money on the game for you if you truly want to experience the game for yourself.
EDIT:For some reason steam finds it offensive if I use the poopoo word, so I edited that part.

Overall, I would say it's a below-average game that I wouldn't recommend paying $20 for. I don't think the ending is good enough to justify how many boring and mediocre scenes it takes to get there. I would only recommend it if you get it when it's free like I did.

Matiss7
8 products in account
0
No one has rated this review as helpful yet 0

Not Recommended
0.5 hrs on record
Posted: 19 January, 2024
I will be honest here, I haven't gotten off the ferry yet in this game before it became too insufferable to continue. The dialogue just feels... off? There is really poor pacing and the voice actor on Tyler speaks without much feeling, almost monotone. Just reading off his script, nothing more.

I like DontNod and this company has such nostalgic feeling games that I can't but love them, despite their flaws. However this game just doesn't do it. The nostalgic feeling their games are known for was present in this game, and it made me push through some of the early dialogue, to no avail. One example about how off it feels is that they are a brother and a sister that have been separated for ten years, whilst obviously sharing a past they feel like complete strangers AND like they have never been separated. When they first meet again outside of the (I assume) mental health institution, they are both pretty constrained, not knowing how to interact with one another. And that's fine, that's fully understandable. You have been away from each other for ten years, you do not know each other as well as you used to. But then, as soon as they start talking they suddenly start acting like best mates. If you make your characters start off shy and restrained, don't make them suddenly do a 180 and make them very comfortable around each other. The ferry could've been a nice moment to explore what their dynamic could be, and how they can reconcile after all these years. Instead it is wasted on wish washy nothingness? It is lost potential of a very interesting dynamic, of two siblings bonding after a shared traumatic past.

I wouldn't pick this up, it doesn't have the DontNod trademarked feel, it rather feels like you are listening to voice actors saying their lines in the mic instead of in-game characters communicating with one another. The pacing is off and the conversations are just weird and feel unnatural. Can't recommend it, I rather suggest you play your tenth run of Life is Strange.

0
No one has rated this review as helpful yet
1 person found this review funny 0

Not Recommended
16.5 hrs on record
Posted: 4 January, 2022
Product received for free

If you get it for free, it's alright. Go watch this movie-walkthru. Otherwise, don't bother. There are better games out there, and better movies, too.

Tell me why I should play this game
The plot of Tell Me Why seems narrow, the playable characters are caught in a simplistic right/wrong mentality. Choices are no real choices but rather some clicks to push the plot forward. Dialogue options are unclear, and so are the consequences of some actions you take during this game drama. Achievements are unlocked simply by your continuing to play - 'hurray! you made it to chapter II, congrats!' The puzzles are so easy it's exaggerated to call them puzzles at all. The ones at the end are the only ones where you actually have to think (but not too hard,don't get upset ;)

Tell me why I should believe my choices matter
Keep away if you're not so much into political correctness, transgender issues, moralistic behavior, self-righteousness, emotional slavery, and the blame game. After a while it gets quite annoying. Oh yes, environmentalism and ethnic minority issues also play a role, and i think it's a great idea.

Unfortunately, the profundity and relevance of these noble ideas gets muddled by the same ideological claptrap and new woke mentality that seems to be the red thread of the game. I found it difficult to empathize with the characters. They both get offended so incredibly fast (especially Tyler). They get upset for reasons that imho do not justify their 'righteous anger'. Overall, both Tyler and Alyson seem to be inclined to make others responsible for how they feel.

Did i mention there are no real choices? Wouldn't be a problem if the game wouldn't pose as if there were. Therefore, i was sometimes reluctant to continue. But i craved another achievement and i ain't no quitter so i continued - oh how easy it is to be manipul8ed... makes me so angry ;) L0L

Tell me why it's still worth giving it a try
Ok, seriously now. What's good about the game? Well, first of all I got it for free which is as it should be cuz I'd never pay for this tbh. Another argument to play is simply cuz it's a DontNod thingie. Because it's beautifully crafted, graphics are impeccably polished, details are a pleasure to behold. And because i had a good laugh when the biggest manipulator in town calls his father a manipulator. Hilarious, really, and sad, since in his narcissistic attitude he can't fathom the irony of the situation.

Btw, I am the 0% that believes Tom's side of the story.

☀☀ Graphics persuaded me to continue
☀ / ☁ Political correctness sensibilization / indoctrination

☁☁ No Trading Cards

Dodo1248
37 products in account
0
7 people found this review helpful 0

Not Recommended
1.5 hrs on record
Posted: 7 June, 2023
This game/story had so much potential but it fell flat. The whole game is based on the kid’s mom being a bigot and wanting to kill one of the kids because he’s transgender.

The story plays out as the two kids having a horrible childhood filled with joyous memories. Wait…what?
All the two main characters talk about is how horrible their mother was to them but they also talk about the wonderful memories they had growing up.

They go back home to their house where they grew up and were traumatized only to talk about how Tyler hopes whoever buys the home doesn’t demolish it to build something new and safer. He says there are so many grate memories of growing up with a horrible mother who was apparently mentally ill and treated them horribly.

The kids later find out that their mother didn’t care that Tyler is trans but never told him or showed him. This was supposed to be the big twist in the game I think but it doesn’t sit will. If someone loves you, they don’t hide it and make you feel like an outcast. But in order to create drama, the story has to make you think the mom hated Tyler.

It’s sloppy and lazy writing.

There’s a supernatural aspect to the game the story could have focused on instead. The two characters could have spun the story that their mother tried to kill Tyler because she was a bigot while knowing she was possessed by a demon/spirt creature.

The game could have had the two siblings running around trying to find out what happened that night to find out if there is more going on than the townspeople are telling them.

I think it would have been great storytelling if the two main characters were going home to try to figure out really happened with their mom and to stop “the evil” from spreading or affecting someone else.

Don’t bother with this game. Just watch it on YouTube and save yourself a few hours of gameplay.

`_`
86 products in account
0
2 people found this review helpful 0

Not Recommended
3.2 hrs on record
Posted: 15 March, 2021
Dontnod have a talent to build their whole games about a narrative, and at the same time have that narrative be complete piece of dog waste.

While not as disastrous as whatever the hell LiS2 was, this one just wasn't good either. Pacing is once again awful, even more panning shots of silence, even more "flavor" dialogues that taste like tap water, even less choice with consequence, and even less at stake. This game despite featuring a transgender protagonist is not immune to criticism, HELL, I'd say it's worse that their representation is realized in just a really bad game.

Since it's a Dontnod game, we had picking up groceries in 1st ep, instead of collecting bottles, what a "welcome" return of the dullest sections in their games. All locations feature the objects that your character just looks at and comments in the utmost obnoxious and obvious ways. Nothing of value, just like way back when I played LiS1. I almost couldn't believe that terrible formula didn't change at all.
Between that and dialogues about constant reminescing (also featured in all of their ♥♥♥♥♥♥ games), you get choices to make (that are compared to choices of other players), which will give a different animation, dialogue, at best a different scene, mostly of no real consequence. I literally can't believe that the devs decided to devolve their gameplay ever since 1st game, Sands of Time rewind in an adventure game was the only thing setting that apart, that and a cop-out of an impactful choice resulting in character's death, or survival (if she survived, you got just one scene with her near the end, phenomenal, ground-breaking).
So in LiS2 and Tell Me Why, such a big thing is not there at all, neither a real mechanic, or a choice of similar level. In both you decide the ending in the last episode, just like you can decide to be a communist mass murderer in LiS 1, in order to save your selfish waifu.
Here you get to decide, the events of the past? It's weird, but the characters power is remembering stuff wrong, and then deciding which is right (sometimes it's just simply wrong, without a choice). They also have telepathy, nothing original with it, they just can communicate over short distance, instead of needing to whisper to their ears.
The characters are also once again ranging from annoying, to dumb, to surface level, to literal straw-men, to walking contradictions. You can only get snippets of good things about their writing, in the bigger picture - they're just tools, whose personality is just their member berries about the past they can't stop spewing throughout the game.
Funnily enough, the locations on later episodes are reused all the time, and also the siblings here are represented by goblins, copied from sibling wolves in LiS2, really makes it feel all the more fresh.

The sounds are there, nothing special, you will 98% of the time just hear yapping. Music is ambient, mixed with the alternative bands copyright stuff sprinkled here and there. Once again, very original, never before done in their game.

The visuals is the only thing I have real praise for, the improvements are huge. The face textures finally don't look like a muddy PS2 mess. Animations are better, environments as well, probably mocap was used, since faces are the most striking difference during the playthrough.

So, I played 1st ep for free, saw rest of the game on playthroughs online. Anyone can play the first ep really, see what they think about it. Rest of it is definitely not worth the money, seeing it done 3rd time in a row, really makes me think that LiS 3 will once again be cut from the same template, with once again - nothing worthwhile added.
BUT - most importantly, I would rather see next 1000 copies bought of Tell Me Why, than see another one purchase of LiS 2.

magik88285
0
No one has rated this review as helpful yet 0

Not Recommended
7.9 hrs on record
Posted: 13 December, 2023
As much as I wanted to love "Tell Me Why," I can't ignore the glaring flaws in its storytelling that ultimately overshadow its visually appealing graphics. The game's stunning aesthetics draw you in from the start, but sadly, the narrative fails to deliver on the same level.

The plot feels contrived and lacks the emotional depth I was hoping for. The characters' motivations and actions often come across as forced, leaving me detached from their struggles. The attempt to explore complex themes falls short, and instead of engaging with genuine emotional weight, the narrative feels like a checklist of clichés.

Moreover, the pacing is inconsistent, with some scenes dragging on unnecessarily while others rush through potentially impactful moments. It's as if the writers couldn't decide on the tone they wanted, resulting in a disjointed and unsatisfying experience.

The dialogue, despite attempts to tackle serious issues, often comes off as forced and unnatural. The characters' interactions feel scripted, preventing any meaningful connection with the player. The lack of depth in character development makes it difficult to empathize with their struggles, and the dialogue choices, which should enhance the experience, often feel inconsequential.

Despite these narrative shortcomings, I can't deny the game's visual excellence. The attention to detail in the environments, character models, and animations is commendable. The graphics create a visually immersive world that is unfortunately let down by a lackluster narrative.

In the end, "Tell Me Why" is a prime example of a game where style triumphs over substance. While the graphics showcase the potential for a memorable gaming experience, the weak storytelling diminishes the overall impact. It's disheartening to see such a visually stunning game fall short in delivering a compelling and engaging narrative.

Not Recommended
9.3 hrs on record
Posted: 4 November, 2023
This game is terrible even for FREE.

I've completed it and it was a chore! The game is very slow and very boring. A slow-burner - also should really be called a film and not a game because of how little actual game-play there is and how little control over characters you get. However I decided to finish it as the plot was promising. With some supernatural elements in the game I hoped for at least half-decent (if not really good) story. Well I was waiting and waiting until ending hit me in my face. What I got was a boring, predictable story with terrible ending.

More details of my thoughts:
- Game consists of 90% cut scenes and 10% actual game-play (more or less) and actual game-play is...
- Actual game-play is so slow! Characters do everything super slow! They talk slow, they walk slow (there is only 1 map your character is allowed to jog - everywhere else you just slowly stroll), they look at things slow. My god this was so annoying and the worst part was that...
- You cannot skip anything! You cannot skip whole cut scene and you cannot even skip a dialogue line. If you accidentally click on the same answer you have to listen to everything again! This is just terrible! Sometimes when I want to speed things up (usually when dialogue bores me) I read subtitles and skip without character finish talking. Here you cant skip anything.
- The Game is full of stupid, dull and unnecessary tasks which only add to slowness of the game. For instance you need to manually count products on the shelves or you have to bring few objects to NPC even though it would be 100% faster for him to just grab it as it is 5 meters away from him.
- I read some comments that the game speeds up after chapter 1. Believe me it does not! It is super slow from beginning to the end.

In my opinion it was all done on purpose. The game's plot could have been a 1 or 2 hours journey. So the developers tried to prolong it every chance they got. Everything is slow, unskippable and the game is full of dull, unnecessary tasks! And it still ends in few hours

- The worst romance I have ever seen in any game. It is so lame to the point it is pathetic. And guess what you cannot skip any of it you have to sit there and listen to this no matter how much you do not care about it. You have to watch how they look at each other sloooooowly and share their deeeep thoughts. Luckily you are able to turn down your date at the end but... Come on! He is still forced down your thought to become your best friend even tho he was a complete, annoying do*che
- This game tells you that choices matter - this is a lie. Choice does not matter. Tell me Why pretends choice is significant but in reality it does not affect the story and just slightly alters the ending (well not even ending itself - only relations between characters). The choice in this game only comes down to few pictures and words at the end of the story about each character and imo can be ignored. It is a game on rails you will just go with what is scripted. - Invisible walls everywhere you go!
