MunchieS
293 products in account
0
1 person found this review helpful 0

Not Recommended
2.1 hrs on record
Posted: 7 August, 2022
It was a difficult decision to choose to recommend this game or not, as I think it could be very enjoyable for specific players.

This is less a game, and more a storybook with high-end graphics. The story is fixated on a controversial topic - and when I say fixated, I mean strongly. I don't mind if a game wants to include such topics (say, Dragon Age with contemporary sexuality/gender choices available), but this game throws it in your face left and right, up and down whether you like it or not, and you are forced to support it in the storyline. Perhaps the writers want to help others understand the real struggles of people facing gender uncertainty, but it comes across like they are trying to shove it down your throat, much like the those of the conservative or religious POV. I have no opinion here for or against this topic, but if you play this game, this is something you ought to be prepared for.

There is basically no gameplay in this game (like Detroit: Become Human). The *story* is more-or-less fixed, and the most you will be is some puzzle solving. Your dialog decisions don't have much actual impact.

In conclusion, if you want a book with voice acting and really nice visuals, this might be the "game" for you. Otherwise, I think most will find this to be a slow-paced, near-zero-gameplay, game with a controversial theme overpowering what game merit there is to enjoy.

Spoilers ahead.





Boy oh boy, another Life is Strange game, but this time they already poked a hole through the bottom of the barrel, there is literally nothing left.

LiS: Turn back time
LiS2: Wind powers
LiS two brothers: One ages & the other has poltergeist powers when angry
LiS colors: A person knows what Empathy is.
Tell me Why: The ability to remember. (Added bonus of talking to the only twin with your brain.)


This game has an intense parts however they are not intriguing, more of misleading.
You have the ability to remember stuff in detail. but hey, sometimes your memory is not correct... oh boy. and you're trying to remember weather or not your mother tried to kill you.

Do your choices matter? nope! in the end you literally decide what ending you want. the game was way to predictable, I called the ending from the beginning in call with friends, I even solved the puzzle by literally saying "Moose, bear, Goose" thinking I wouldn't get it but I apparently that's the ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥ answer.
I found the diary instantly, the only trouble I had was getting into the house, I was just blind for that moment.

The "Problem" of the game. the main problem of the game is circled around Tyler, the Trans kid. of course. it wouldn't be a LiS game if it didn't have anyone from the LGBTQ, not that it is a problem, it was just predictable.
My problem with the game is not him being trans, but the way they try to represent him as a trans and how it goes along with the game, and it does not quite tie to the ending of the game. (does not need to but hey, character arc is a thing and I believe they just failed to show it.) It ends up like any Netflix show, they (Insert here 1 gay person) and their entire character is just gay. Same for Tyler, He is a trans kid, every argument or sentence has him being trans of some sort.
Which is understandable through some conversations but bringing up in some scenarios is just weird and out of place.
Not only that but when they found the book "How to raise a trans kid" I'm sure that's insulting to some, but others can see that she actually might have tried, and they got angry at it
"What the ♥♥♥♥? my mom is trying to understand me and what I am going through? this is ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥!" pretty much how it is.
The worst part of this, is when they go outside and you're stuck there for five minutes looking at mountains

The entire game is just trying to find your deadbeat dad who left the mother to her two kids who hate her because mommy said "No"
then trying to remember which ending, (You decide since choices don't matter) either she was trying to shoot you for giving you the spiky anime hair. or she was just trying to tell you that she was going to shoot herself in the barn... with a shotgun... so the kids can hear.

TL:DR
Choices don't matter get ♥♥♥♥♥♥ lmao
Super power is rubbing to brain cells together
Deadbeat dad shows up & leaves to get milk again.
first character: Enabler.
Second character: Trans & main attention however still unlikable
No character arc.

I give this game a too/boring

and that was the highlight of this gameplay.
Now I need a name for this mouse.

This is such a bad story game. I played up until I completed the store section with the crazy Bible study lady.

It's about these twins who went through a traumatic childhood, at one point their mother dies. One of the twins is a trans man and believes everything surrounds about him being trans, gets offended about anything and everything, is constantly on edge and is ultimately annoying and difficult to deal with.

The twins have a superpower which makes them able to talk to each other with their mind, without actually talking, and they can find memories and witness them together.

They try to find out why their crazy mother lost her mind at her final days and if it had anything to do with one of the twins being trans. "I thought my mom wanted to kill me because I wanted to be a boy." They investigate places to find out the truth.

The dialogue is awkward, unnatural and badly written. The conversations are so unrealistic, it made my eyes roll quite a couple of times. A lot of items in-game can be inspected and the twins will talk about it, their reactions to stuff takes way too long and I don't care in the slightest.

Out of all the story based games I played, this is the absolute worst I have ever played.

freakytugay
8 products in account
0
7 people found this review helpful 1

Not Recommended
2.0 hrs on record
Posted: 16 May, 2021
Review 2 minutes in:
I'm not sure I can get into this game like I did Life is Strange and Before the storm. Game-play feels sluggish and the characters are kind of dead, if it weren't for the transgender signalling I'd probably enjoy this game more, but hey if you're about that then go right ahead. If only LIS had these kind of graphics though, it'd be awesome.

As far as I can tell I'm probably not going to like this game predominantly for the transgender stuff; now you can call me a transphobe all day long, but I don't really care I'm just saying it because that's my preference. I'm not going into my beliefs or political ideology in this review because it's unfair to the game itself. I will play it just to say I did and to get insight into these characters, but beyond that I probably will not like it as I haven't really enjoyed the direction of LIS games lately. LIS has such a strong place close to my heart because I went through similar stuff, subsequently relating to Chloe Price, and some of the other characters in the game like Kate Marsh, but with the hyper-political environment that is the world today, it's difficult to agree to disagree. I'll leave comments on for those who want to comment about it, but do so in a respectful manner please. I'm not here to fight, but do want to hear opinions.

First Episode Edit (After two hours of game-time):
Yeah... I can't get into this, the first episode is only two hours but it felt like I played for four. I had to grab a cup of coffee half way through. I will give a 10//10 for the graphics, the sounds and the voice acting. All that is pretty decent aside from one characters voice actor.

That being said though, the main characters don't really have much life, and this is coming from someone who has a sister. These two don't act like siblings at all really (Except for their childhood), but once they meet back up it's more like they were friends than siblings. Tyler is kind of the type of character who believes the world revolves around him, especially when it comes to the past. He politically signals a lot and it got kind of annoying to play through with a "Environment this, or politics that, or transgender this." in every piece of dialogue, if he was trying to make jokes it was always drowned out by his personality which did not fit the same jokes he tried to make. He's combative with people who don't support his feelings or his opinions, and at times its entirely unjustified. I found myself liking a lot of the side characters more than him, and that's bad if he's the main character. For comparison, he felt more like a Nathan Prescott than someone we should feel sorry for and try to understand.

Alyson was alright, she was more sensible than Tyler. In ways she was raised differently than him and it shows through some of the choices you can make with her and some of her different memories, mannerisms, dialogue and personality. Of course every choice you don't make in Tylers' favor gains nothing short of his ire and wrath. On the side of memories that's actually pretty accurate between siblings, one will remember different things for better or worse and that was portrayed okish.

Their power The Voice is pretty cool and is a phenomenon that actually has some bearing in real life, I know me and my sister can read each others thoughts with nothing but our facial expressions and there's been scientists who have recorded this special bond between siblings. Which is more to the point of one of the core problems of this game, the two simply do not act like siblings. There's been times me and my sister have had the exact same humor and think the exact same thing when we see something. Hell, we practically have the exact same personality. That connection here feels forced, yet at the same time doesn't even set out to make them feel like they're siblings. It doesn't work. It's rare that me and my sister get into real fights or outright really disagree like these two do in this game, but I understand that might have changed for these characters (I wont spoil it), but me and my sister have a tough love type of relationship. We hardly have genuine conversations outside of making fun of each other or flipping each other off while also being there for each other, It's something I can't explain but can understand when I see it. When we do get serious or have genuine conversations about something it mattered and the other knew it mattered, here in this game it just feels like that sibling element is missing... I did not see it here, maybe a little but it was drowned out by Tyler's personality.

This chapter almost had me during the first hour when Tyler discovers truths about his mother (Again won't spoil), but once again his personality ruins it. The only good thing he does is to try and uncover that truth a little bit, which doesn't fit his personality at all. I would've expected Alyson to be the one wanting to know the truth, not Tyler who spent the last seven odd years hating his mother enough to form preconceived notions about her. When he discovers that they may not be true he goes against his personality to uncover some of the truth while Alyson does not want the truth despite appearing to hate their mother less??? This is supported by some of HER memories which appear to portray their mother as a person and not as an abusive parent like Tyler's does. Anyway it was confusing, their personalities were like split between them at times. You'd expect Tyler to be the one wanting to sell the house as fast as possible since he experienced the worst as a child and clearly hated their mother more, not Alyson...

There isn't much humor, and any that is there, is clearly political or even anti-offense humor... Makes it a snooze fest. This is worse when you realize there had been pretty much only one or two songs played in the entire first episode, at least the ones I noticed. It was eerily silent at times, and there weren't any scenes where you could just chill and vibe to a unique soundtrack like in LIS. Some of the ambient sounds were pretty nice and realistic and not overly done.

The puzzles, don't even get me started on that. I had to grab my reading glasses just to try and wrap my head around it as I read the same page four times over... They're too complex and make me roll my eyes whenever I see one. Not to mention the game forces you to read children stories for clues to these puzzles, thank god I could force my way past it but I know that is likely not the case for any other ones in the other episodes.

The decisions also suck, they're black and white and have no real effect, or weight other than a brash comment, political woke signal, or outright aggressive response from Tyler. "ReSpeCtK mY FeElinGs PHobE." is what I feel every time I hear Tyler's voice in the back ground.

But yeah... I'd rather play life is strange AND before the storm ten times over than another episode of this game... Which means I'm probably not going to buy the other two episodes if they're all like this...

Overall I'd give it a 4/10 and it's only that high for the graphics...

Product received for free

In this game you play Tyler. The trans brother of your identical twin sister Alyson. I didn’t remember that when I finally played the game. When I learned that I was trans, I felt betrayal. As in I betrayed myself, my friends, sister, family, god, the world and everything. That was Interesting. Still I power forward.

The ferry ride was the best part of the game. Just watching the scenery. But I go and ruin it by having an awkward conversation with a rando who knew my parents. Having grown up having to explain my real world family to people, I knew several ways that conversation would have been natural. But not for me in this game. My character made this awkward. But, I go forward anyway.

Next childhood trauma is revealed as a major focus in the game. I don’t enjoy that. In flashbacks my younger self was acting out in ways that didn’t make sense. I was causing a lot of my own misery. Which I didn’t connect with. But I powered forward.

Flashbacks don’t use your given name. They use “Young Tyler” or Ollie. Both of which are true in their use. However neither was your actual name at the time. Your younger self hadn’t even thought up Tyler yet, so while "Young Tyler" is accurate, it’s not apt. I wanted to know where I came from and the light the game shines on my characters past is missing this simple thing. But forward I go.

Not long after that I’m having a flashback to a bonding moment between sisters. Alyson says something like “You are the best sister” to which nameless me replies. “I feel like I’m your brother”. At this point I pause and I look back on my own life and realize that I never once felt like my sibling’s brother. I just was their brother. After that I lost interest in the game. More accurately I lost interest playing Tyler. He’s too much of a twit. I’d rather have played his sister.

Here's why I don't like this game(I was on a call with my brother while playing):

First of all, I did not know anything about this game when I got it. The only reason why I have it is because it was free. As a pirate of the internet, this has appealed to me. I downloaded it and realized that why they made it free.

When Tyler and the sister(can't even bother to remember her name) first meet each other, my guess was that they were going to have magical super powers that allow them to sense, feel, or hear each other from far away. I was pretty on point.

When Tyler was trying to take off the planks to get under the house, I said this to my brother: "Oh noooo! I'm too weak to take off these planks! If only there were a tutorial on how to use my powers, then maybe I could find a way through!" In case you haven't played this game, there was a tutorial afterwards explaining how to use your powers to get the screwdriver.

Every time that the sister started yapping as I search the outside, I had to go to the audio settings and turn voices all the way down. I literally could not hear her for any longer if her dialogue has nothing to with what I'm doing or the current plot.

In these types of games, they like to bloat it with "lore" and "environmental storytelling." I'm not the type of person to listen if it has no purpose, so I try to guess which parts actually continued the story and didn't just fill it up with literally nothing. First of all, when you enter a house to collect something, go upstairs. Ignore bathrooms and closets and head for hard to miss doors. When you enter a room, look for containers. The thing you are looking for will always be hidden in a box or drawer. This piece of advice actually helped me solve the first puzzle as quickly as possible, but I genuinely hate how it worked so well.

After I obtained Tyler's diary, I was super bored. The music and visuals try to make me feel something, but I feel nothing. This is when I said that I would play this game tomorrow. Here I am, writing a review instead of playing. I am pretty sure that I guessed more things about this game within the first few minutes, but I have forgotten if those events even happened at all. This game is extremely forgettable. I probably will not notice that I own this game until years later.

Here's what I actually liked about this game:

The sister had a working mirror in her room. I might replay the start of the game just to have a look at how great that mirror looks compared to other games.

As a lover of AI generated nightmares, this game feels like it heavily influenced how AI generates their stories. That may be because of their hidden bias and how they are always supporters of the LGBTQ+. This game doesn't feel AI generated, but AI generation feels like it came from this game.

0.4 hrs on record
Posted: 1 November, 2022
If your looking for a review on this game you've come to the wrong place, but if your're looking for an outstanding pie recipe you've come to the right place.

Ingredients:
1. 6 tablespoons unsalted butter
2. 1/2 cup white sugar
3. 1/2 cup brown sugar
4. 1/4 cup water
5. 1/4 teaspoon cinnamon
6. 1 pinch salt
7. 5 apples - peeled, cored and sliced
8. 1 pastry for double-crust pie

Directions:
1. Preheat oven to 425 degrees F (220 degrees C).
2. Combine butter, white sugar, brown sugar, water, cinnamon, and salt in a saucepan over medium heat. Bring to a boil, remove from heat and set aside.
3. Roll out half the pastry to fit a 9-inch pie plate. Place bottom crust in pie plate; pour in apple slices.
4. Roll out top crust into a 10-inch circle. Cut into 8 (1-inch) wide strips with a sharp paring knife or pastry wheel. Weave the pastry strips, one at a time, into a lattice pattern. Fold the ends of the lattice strips under the edge of the bottom crust and crimp to seal.
5. Pour butter-sugar mixture over top of pie, coating the lattice, and allowing any remaining sauce to drizzle through the crust.
6. Bake in the preheated oven for 15 minutes. Reduce heat to 350 degrees F (175 degrees C), and bake until the crust is golden brown, the caramel on the top crust is set, and the apple filling is bubbling, 35 to 40 more minutes. Allow to cool completely before slicing.
